Time Inc. & "The New"


As the magazine publishing business continues to find ways to streamline and evolve to the "multi-platform" world, that will inevitably mean a lot of job cuts. That was the impetus behind Time Inc. CEO Laura Lang's decision to layoff 480 employees -- 6 percent of its 8,000-person staff -- across most of its business units. In a company-wide memo obtained by Adweek's Lucia Moses, the former Digitas executive told staffers, "We need to operate as smartly and efficiently as possible to create room for critical investments and new initiatives. These reductions are part of this important transformation process." Read more <http://r20.rs6.net/tn.jsp?e=001Q6N6Fuh79zFwfNb7_pj9z0rehUQ_yurgm1gCDhJomqpBv7WnTIO7tqavEk0pSWkIS2izCPsHke9_ZdRVsuGz_tD0XvWTDs0Q8mSDOBRxFNLW1NSe9Yjx7eaYlPgzkLw90sk89j8SfIau6xNkKKFzzA-XJ-NOZObUD9hO8oRp8_XB8pOWphDWgQg6Ta6_-RptftxZ2eLfR1c=> . 


Mobile Cookie


Display ad platform OpenX has teamed up with device recognition software provider AdTruth on an ad targeting solution for mobile real-time bidding. Read the release <http://r20.rs6.net/tn.jsp?e=001Q6N6Fuh79zE-oDX2_U8FrDGdoNInNo8PBADJnMERnhhnm10bEVJXEsXoNQTg48c7PPJSuTL44tfjsk0PrzODOv9OVw-T9igQwsCYB6WciI_E1mulKhVH4e-duoh5ekVVZiv41wNprDcTfTT9FAYVjK2iJZqwW5VjhC-GHBjn3nQk_N4cTgO43ukw6BL_xkiOHz481xL1Ql5hsxWWyoHA5Nf52j1z9thhWDjylmaThZtSSrD_zlDqgg==> . After all, one of the major problems is the difficulty in tracking smartphone and tablet users through cookies. So the companies that can best direct their inventory towards the right audiences will be the ones driving ad spending in the space, as RTB growth rates generally slow down <http://r20.rs6.net/tn.jsp?e=001Q6N6Fuh79zEzkGgOhK-tGaJLG0Ay9uj6QzsnY-j91yfis5t4UFRticBrKtWnvptczMpkspXKkNhEUp9XeEzSwHvPL9dQe3ni9qOQPIjvHKCH3Q_SELSnaf2ZSYi4ApK8Hcu681fg27jBN5nrynCxTOASl57M85e1OyOT3Y1ulEVOwG5XH6JMhVcB0e2nWdwP> . As Mike Downey, VP of OpenX's mobile solutions, explains in a blog post, "Essentially, AdTruth will fill the gap where cookies do not perform, ultimately resulting in increased ROI for the marketer." Read more <http://r20.rs6.net/tn.jsp?e=001Q6N6Fuh79zFtsxiquhkgrOwY7dn_El1b8NvU5qwMjAxcaMW2-i5lWTYDePO-4ckkVjzacnyltrmG09Fzb7hnOtOAbHF4PTBKcyue94pXo0zJ3xcmOUzc6muBjvTem4eRkq8UA6SYz7Itp22m2O-RRVAVfqu79N2lKHFp3C-WalA=> . 


Data Quality, Not Quantity


Marc Guldimann, founder and CEO of first-party data provider Enliken, believes that the industry debate over "more data" versus "better data" is a false one. In a blog post on AllThingsD, he contends that despite gathering greater amounts of data through more tracking cookies placed on sites, analytics companies still can't tell whether a user is male or female. His answer: "Instead of scraping as many touchpoints as possible, we could go straight to the source: The individual. Imagine the power of data from across an individual's entire digital experience - from search to social to purchase, across devices. This kind of data will make all aspects of online advertising more efficient: True attribution, retargeting-type performance for audience targeting, purchase data, customized experiences." Read more <http://r20.rs6.net/tn.jsp?e=001Q6N6Fuh79zH6Rvc5AthMOSP7432hq_OYebXCe3ZQoT6IvOgr2piwy9q0_A-AUnuOrQ2YquZ_l0AEtvl-ffx9vc-nN9FBs_YWy-3buu6mdmQ6yHws59OzTl1JDWYMQoVnToqFf_BvA-HAuuxBTPKgm2OO8k-EcNOWQMyL2hArLXsFNAI24iH3Dd-hC1yNURjDZ3bQTx6jLxG_CkYeQ3KQLhg0LIL8AfZbS5DR--Ls2os=> . 


Teasing RTB


CEO Ed Montes of trading desk Digilant "teases" out his thesis about the transformative effects of real-time bidding (RTB) on advertising. He does see some downside, though: "1) the cost to deploy RTB effectively is significant, both from a hardware and human resource capacity and 2) RTB deployed without prophylactic computing power can lead to corrupt behavior." Did he just say "prophylactic"? Read it <http://r20.rs6.net/tn.jsp?e=001Q6N6Fuh79zFdjHxz8o_mlSUCydBLNY38OpXq6MgYw8f5BUGFUNdiiuF2mbg5q03Uk51IUecFLE88ZCbVklHO5Scp6xCK5IT4bCmKEYXgkOEV9yB9uD1xpME_8WYXBRD5aQ1sHYdwKg2GVZ5xQeCDsSEJJ0FG7N8yZ0-104ApjR5_t6WgsSd_yU1hQM4psHLY3MEzRbZUG7UcAzDMEaTE_w==> . 


Facebook's CPG Pitch


A recent Facebook dog-and-pony show for CPG brands was the first of several upcoming events aimed at specific ad verticals. AdAge reports executives showcased the "Custom Audiences" CRM matching program, and despite CMO complaints about Facebook's ad policies and some issues with sales strategy, brands were all ears. "I think the attitude is what matters, and they have that willingness to improve," said Reckitt Benckiser Chief Strategy and Marketing Officer Laurent Faracci. More.  <http://r20.rs6.net/tn.jsp?e=001Q6N6Fuh79zG1DZiI7S4yE2WKu5h61FMbICpYT336fq4Sp-AFOe8trPxtceniCq1_lutJMxvWNEVhZrio2uZDIBbQENd9CoD2WwJoJwAYAH6xacfv9G6YBTs0hYB83wcSFIOMjCVtDEDDwKfxGNo8HbMbSdHLrD3mtWZtpu1TXmDmzcVHb4YasA==>

Ad Inventory Force


In a post on Adrants, Joe Pych, CEO of software analytics firm NextMark, argues that ad tech vendors "force fit" ad inventory into a transaction process that ignores the human element that creates deals between buyers and sellers. Aside from the fact that agencies "make a ton of money" on reserved inventory buys the old-fashioned way, publishers remain nervous about giving up choice placements. "Publishers are certainly keen to streamline their workflow, lower their transaction costs," Pych says. "However, they will never do that in an environment that commoditizes their inventory and creates channel conflict with their ad sales teams." Read more <http://r20.rs6.net/tn.jsp?e=001Q6N6Fuh79zGLKA1d85S_2yA8rnv9XpBbyckvYJPGGB4CR0UKKU6_mMXy1oyp6VQgEqK0DxGpI_fjj7cXGUJOGh9Pb3KKsOw3Glf8W9HCYVRfstJYt6jvz_PQv7-iMD08OH4DLzfRaW_p3QbMkM9S9TDjOpcori1LGmzJ6c2U8hwRwCiCjU6cWg==> .

E-Commerce's Easy Gains


Trade group National Retail Federation projects growth for online sales will rise between 9% and 12% this year, compared to total retail sales gains - which are in the 3.4% growth range. Still, NRF analysts say the uncertain economy could dull digital sales increases. "While it's too early to know the full effect of higher payroll taxes, there's no question that many consumers will feel some kind of impact from the change in their paychecks," says Jack Kleinhenz, the NRF's chief economist. Read the release <http://r20.rs6.net/tn.jsp?e=001PMZ5NuBAalHfFh6ZEwHQh6wyq1rTBbORsL3u6cOp_bqFbEGnq6jLalHXVpMor3XsDxHtOtmUzOnEp8jRKsF1Tlur0dmX1yVXuxpJN27ifxc-MIX1CNCdMTZ_tfskNxZRj8M6qb6k_yN4LwSrlQzwHx0rjbP9fyGvLV8E5omus6yW4-lTandsgg==> . Another reason RTB buying will grow? 


Waiting For Amazon


Amazon is the "Waiting for Godot" of ad tech companies -- or maybe it's just the Amazon of ad tech companies. The secretive titan is still quietly ramping up its data-driven ad platform, reports the Financial Times, with placements happening on both O&O and off-site properties. FT's Emily Steel does get a rare quote, as Amazon Media Group sales chief Lisa Utzschneider tells her, "We've been heads down, focused on building an advertising offering and solution that is right for marketers and right for our customers." Read more <http://r20.rs6.net/tn.jsp?e=001PMZ5NuBAalF0Jg1JoWAOXUL3oTrqem0kI7JRIOgJQkBxSIoQwU2fYVeNInPBjUMSIvhI4HVdtDJfd6zljMWf9xIVJiganJ80gWaQ1xBIg3A8nXWb7j5faorUd88p0ac11mmslrurCXp38ofy380TqrY0MWjb9C60XHIEsjDCrId9z9MbOuyVCM35h1cuQ6OwGLrFfhHu2ln0dGuysXm3dg==> . (registration required) And, see yesterday's earnings release from AMZN <http://r20.rs6.net/tn.jsp?e=001PMZ5NuBAalEp3IQx7OZ9XjyCxc2CHYTbvc4q6wBZAXLEqy5z6wVSuWbYHs5mj7hCeBUNOTZuJTx8O0TTa5BEdC55Dk2b013UeKIzzKc4SE-4GmL3Apfd-CH_E9d6o75bFgCi97tKtWSADhQrYg8t7vX0w5nTyzgBGexkFzWWxAP4Ml2QfVLmHPYJ5AnQyXeIesKIcFlrsJ4-kpMpDjY8ptJwC2pcbRRb> . 


Social Influx


For every brand that goes "all in" with social media, such as a Fab.com, there is a General Motors that turns up its nose - and plenty of others that just take it slow. But 2013 may bring some velocity, according to a survey from Vizu and Nielsen. The data suggests the year will deliver increases of 1 to 10% in social ad budgets, and in some cases significantly more. Where will the dollars come from? Forty-one percent said social spending will be incremental, 39% said it will poach from offline channels, and 33% said digital (display + rich media/video) will suffer. Download the report. <http://r20.rs6.net/tn.jsp?e=001PMZ5NuBAalHfLGUE2HYq0wBsvI2U3WA_UNTk9F-fIUh5L4BwMZDIeunFho25CKbuWNEMjXFmp5JoLJLrWiJapgW-FzN-4jiM3xegSEjxs34g9r4p59I7NcQJVFpS_Sv3jacTReRfWPdkZwqYm63KXTDpyPJhvhoUYAH72uVXIJuSfKpGKXk6otMM41e8d0qAjn4vGTj6Se_zv_Q-9bOuoQAsxLhommM0iHHymNeSTA0=>  (Pay with some PII) 


Rubicon's Revolving Door


The Rubicon Project's latest executive moves have promoted more talk about a possible IPO filing drawing closer. COO/CFO Brian Barnum and Chief Revenue Officer Nick Hulse are both on the way out and SocialVibe CEO Todd Tappin and Dragon Media chief Greg Raifman are on the way in. Tappin will replace Barnum, while Raifman has been named president. "Greg and Todd are extremely intelligent and capable executives who have guided significant, publicly traded companies," said Rubicon founder/CEO Frank Addante to AllThingsD's Kara Swisher. "Both Greg and Todd have great relationships within our industry as well as on Wall Street. Their presence will enable me to focus on our overall vision and product strategy so we can take best advantage of the opportunities we see." Read more <http://r20.rs6.net/tn.jsp?e=001PMZ5NuBAalEtyj5DyEYeXoBT3oP1Y7cfYPC0ZpSn_cm9aTcNmW8nJhB1Mc_-43XKpF49j8RwwgEGq_CHp2E9OM5PNSDfG3_yhemA8WUbavATOjOtuaYDfc73x9MO7is4hmAqILlcc3-CmvyFRWtIpIoSNtnwrAvuVfEF63xJL6yb8idYhZyWgSznIsvJUvyYa8avlCg-2D6BaM7YBzwIofygFrx3OhSg> . 


Buying A Good Reputation


Reputation.com, a company that offers consumers the chance to cleanse the web of nasty photos and dishonorable mentions, has acquired a UK rival, Reputation 24/7. A company spokeswoman told TechCrunch's Natasha Lomas that it would be investing "millions [GBP] over the next year to support the UK branch's expansion - in both capabilities and hiring." Read it. Meanwhile, Michael Fertik, founder and CEO of Reputation.com, told The Liverpool Daily Post (Reputation 24/7's hometown paper) that his goal was to help his new property "dominate" the UK market. What Goes Up, Keeps Going Up


Five-year-old software analytics developer DataGravity has raised a whopping $30 million second round funding led by Andreessen Horowitz. The capital raise comes just just over six months after the Nashua, NH-based startup raised $12 million. "DataGravity is positioned to be in front of a potentially enormous market, and the management team's technical and operational expertise has the experience to lead it. For me, that's an unbeatable value proposition," says Peter Levine, a partner at Andreessen Horowitz. Read the release <http://r20.rs6.net/tn.jsp?e=001PMZ5NuBAalFtnOed1gOw5ZQKkFV-I0aOYfFRkrAXbUwBE7DjkReYkxZV6cZr3PVxIXMb0k-IUUMRQrI3plg1uFPBfopboVdJ_sfqW08gXuczYKOlVgefwhnTqcgXh7ccvg4N_XygMBSG2EyfeRD9sh4WLvnkDWCkUmEYgxbFER9hhu5osyAuzEp838A0a4njSoCCwPQVaZqa2MobJpGMv3Pg7qaqY3cSZ8TQ1Mkrbh8=> . 


Real-Time Mobile


Trading desk Accordant Media says it's installing online mobile apps on behalf of clients to provide them unique opportunities around cross-channel targeting on a real-time basis. Accordant pitches that their solution is "designed for marketers to test into web-based and in-app mobile solutions with clear results and insights - through one reporting source and a single service team." $4 Billion In Spend


Wired covers new research <http://r20.rs6.net/tn.jsp?e=001PMZ5NuBAalGpZTSd2ERgYIK822PRA8mbeKYHb7E7jFBfmGo0UXs3dbPClRUCbRxmK6IPaawr-WK9p8jxv41LW-ZjLe4qJcDSelHUO8sD0b_1Xiax4CTYMq6Ee7zqXwboUJ5Cv0uQqh7tVfW9S6CqfLwC0lUQwjlVnWRe1POMHEfHhw5ZMCWwqnui03gk-l8BkSj-wuMbbEM=>  from buying platform Marin Software on Google Product Listing ads - and discusses the voluminous spend pulsing through its system - mostly search engine marketing-related. Wired's Marcus Pohlsen writes, "Marin Software found that advertisers managing $4 billion annually in online ad campaigns through its platform spent 600 percent more on Google product listing ads after the change in October than before. That result alone doesn't necessarily surprise: If Google says pay to play, advertisers have little choice." Twitter's Ad API Arrival?


For the past three years, Twitter has been saying it's going to release an advertising API. Well, according to anonymous ad executives who speak to Techcrunch's Ingrid Lunden, that moment will finally arrive some time this quarter. "I have been in discussions with Twitter and they contacted us right before the holidays saying it was getting close to having their advertising API ready," one executive told Techcrunch. It's not clear though if Twitter's ad API will be separate from its general tech platform, as Facebook does, or if it will somehow be tightly integrated with the whole. Read more <http://r20.rs6.net/tn.jsp?e=001QOp-Yy0_c9gx_rSS0nyb24RUkx4K7i-eQgHN4uriqpGAspzMY_q5HRofCEb8if3JPiV_ivTWngw4SgBdFtrO_p0wl819iTBSnw0D4JnPdOyOOj1DbyPPxUlFou_crrPxEc8ceAUZXbhfGO8Fu4D8rTr3KEJGb3xg_hYmhrn8smyj5QdlP8wO_OyRV7YRSgcAkuNnkwF85oNy9qepXVXkjiJ7Oiyp8mjs2oiBKg1SSSSEnUNjEFspXg==> . 


My Agency, My Systems Integrator


Razorfish grew significantly last year, not only on the strength pure "marketing," says AdAge. "CTOs and CIOs frequently hire Razorfish for projects, creating new revenue streams that -- even in the face of dwindling ad budgets -- woefully few shops are capturing." That puts the Publicis digital shop in company with the enviable likes of SapientNitro, Cognizant, and Globant. Billings grew 20% to $60 million on the strength of several big wins (Samsung, Target, Uniqlo) and incremental business from Delta, Ford, Mercedes-Benz, Microsoft and Nike. Razorfish made AdAge's "Agency A-List." Facebook Is The New Broadcast


For many marketers, the central idea of social media is that you can slice and dice your desired audience with ease. But for consumer packaged goods, who are looking more for brand awareness, scale is the name of the game. Laurent Faracci, U.S. chief strategy and marketing officer of Reckitt Benckiser, speaking at Facebook's first CPG Summit, was there to say that the social network was the new mass medium all on its own. "The Facebook effort is part of a broader push by Mr. Faracci to rethink how RB goes about marketing, structures its staff, manages agency relations and evaluates results," AdAge's Jack Neff wrote. "That includes moving from a purely cost- and reach-focused 'efficiency' drive to a broader look at efficiency plus effectiveness.'" Read the rest <http://r20.rs6.net/tn.jsp?e=001QOp-Yy0_c9h_KxzOWYobW0Zy5bdOfHIn9nLcS1nOvGdc5gZljV6UVWOfwgfaf10Jqy4gHI-S18qaeglVcuY2IaguEjW3baxAYHto6bKawkEhGqEboxHGmyfcuCoywq8IuomX-Cif0wf2gOPnYWCdxCItnsGKhfBrhRDPfscWCLDiIlJILTwmazpA5xzfp7RlC1zYGX8fhZTwltRUzqdKtRxhHEh--Fx4> .

Customize That Pre-Roll


Gannett's rich media ad provider PointRoll has launched three interactive in-stream video packages, including: Social, Branding and Video AdChooser. The idea is to make it a little easier for marketers to add still more interactivity and customization to their standard in-stream video ad campaigns. "Whether advertisers would like to incorporate branding elements or simply enable consumers to select the ad of their choosing, our turnkey packages are a simple, cost-efficient way to increase engagement for your next in-stream video campaign," said Todd Pasternack, VP, Digital Innovation, PointRoll. Read the release <http://r20.rs6.net/tn.jsp?e=001QOp-Yy0_c9hAx-gJkwTvwWLqlLrlhFjY5gK0_afRETqI1EMMdfTY7xB1vvvF7Zl2QHcFAxMigsBcRkk5wou58qdoKRErIM2p-i8P0Fdcn8sx47otEWEWMB76K8TkI86KNQu5S0QBHiFuFxs8FQ-ewk8VBJsJdjNx8bIul5dqZQ6JpHxwqBw7Gq5LbaiCibPuHIMVtvSkupd-pId5V_oZiujCTs2bY5fe6vX2Ca9jWKy8eHX-Xtvrh2XOE0bYhdhs> .

Mobile Meals


More of us are using mobile apps to get fed, says IAB/Viggle research pegged to the annual snack & ads (oh yeah, and football) blitz known as the Super Bowl. Most interesting here: almost as many consumers are downloading restaurant specific apps as are installing "aggregators" like Seamless and Yelp. Of the 67% who have ordered via mobile, half downloaded a chain specific app while 55% have used things like Urbanspoon and Zagat. Coming soon: edible phones. (Skip the middle man!) Free Video Ad Serving Here


Google is trying to disrupt the world of video advertising - too! On the DoubleClick for Publishers blog, the company announces that its free display ad server will now include free video ad serving. DoubleClick-er Andrew Kuo writes, "Video ad serving is free up to 400K ad impressions a month. Until April 30th, we're offering a free unlimited trial, so you can serve as many video ads as you want. After this trial offer has ended, impressions over 400K a month will be charged a nominal ad serving fee on a CPM basis." Read more. <http://r20.rs6.net/tn.jsp?e=001QOp-Yy0_c9hXZgYVQPSqtc5uzYpg11xRy7_YDhdkhgXQ2ExXoRArBna20EhyycLfvucpsE5vLRejXm9QoxyNLmAhtUSoVbd37Jrn6MLjNz9uCqULD8tvjeshOe3S4QA8HGrOi-rmLaCQsLdDli8rUCtTQsNmdEk9WrSBc3ClD-dI3WWxhYGV7jc3VO9Gv9m5UFjKMZAwu1o=>  And, new cheaper AdWords API pricing, too. <http://r20.rs6.net/tn.jsp?e=001QOp-Yy0_c9iO0TWjXS3avolRsqyH_QhtdGA0JH3sslZCy_SS1I3b4JmIUNUEzG--Q2kVzpPUfFKm4eoakrxRRr6P-OzTtItOaN96f4X1aTWjcsMw2ZOlRAhpWzo9HYpTK3EiCOzSilS_Cn2D-tPes8GKEpUNjfH8lXyM_0beikJb-ONz5OEv7mX907KJTb7LoyPMV7xXgmY=>  Ad verification, tag management, video ad serving.. all free from Google. But are they the same high octane that large advertisers require? Service remains a differentiator for ad tech vendors let alone a deeper feature set. 


Graph Search Signal


On ClickZ, GroupM Next CEO Chris Copeland takes his turn at Facebook's Graph Search. Questions remain for Copeland, "For Graph Search to flourish people will need to engage with brands on a much greater scale then they do at present. I do not doubt the connection numbers that Facebook cites in the Graph Search launch. I am suspect about the quality of brand interactions that can provide meaningful signals and guidance to fellow graph connections."  News Round-Up <http://ih.constantcontact.com/fs116/1102602719219/img/94.jpg>  

Here's today's AdExchanger news round-up... Want it by email?

Meaningless Reach?


How many billions of impressions does your (take your pick) DSP/SSP/DMP etc. process every day? Adweek's Mike Shields offers a rundown of the big platforms, including AppNexus, The Rubicon Project, Turn and others and finds nothing but confusion in the triumphal pronouncements of these companies' reach. "After a while these numbers do two things," Shields says. "They constantly serve to remind people that there are way too many online ads being served, which is why far too few of them to be worth much of anything. And it serves to make one's eyes glaze over-since the reach, impression volume and targeting numbers cease to mean anything. In effect, they get cheapened." Read more <http://r20.rs6.net/tn.jsp?e=001i9JdMEOyUSRuv3brtX4pmFDJ54iPtH4kfpegJ3XLjV4ULqxBablv6mtY6_c6f0_QYi4MA5myA2BtwQxILeO82HLanwV8YXu3v-ZJWcXLkEfPooMa3uJaMDk2MGR52TpxFbqQuVT21tNU9x-GnZGXGe79L0eGacsOWaGLLCFBOk9zbbRq22MRpXFODNze_ZZlSN7oy4uPwAQ=> . 


Yahoo's Portal Partnerships


Yahoo CEO Marissa Mayer's message to attendees at the World Economic Forum in Switzerland last week was to "partner with everyone," including rivals like Google, Facebook and even Apple. But GigaOm's Mathew Ingram isn't buying the strategy and writes ahead of today's Yahoo earnings, "The web portal may still have millions of visitors a month who come to its news pages or other sites, but how does any of that benefit Apple or Google?" Read more <http://r20.rs6.net/tn.jsp?e=001i9JdMEOyUSR5WyTSC6vSOVCVKWXO78zUIxkvg2rZ2u6DF3EHc8NehuHXZT4p20vpTPcc0IJb6qRK4ypAIuVQYBgde4xwBkKtSo1N1NPVCwUTnftLXg6-aS7e1ZoyC3grOjVbDK5PaXkYguzs1AMrl3V1boJHZVx75F98F4H14UrDVfa8SaCOH4aPezJljVHKvsmKddsp3KIT55EXrLPHvyjT59FtiBqCM5XGsS0yX-MFsmtOVCB9qA==> . 


Layoffs


Having taken $39 million in funding, Group Commerce, chaired by former Doubleclick-er David Rosenblatt <http://r20.rs6.net/tn.jsp?e=001i9JdMEOyUSSWBqp2-uXF_AVQMF4ZMHSqVeehvGd-Nwwg7vOUX4AtnGbtshDIkuT83iEOIYFottMy6SnJ4TIkI7v-OwBeGvzcZXA0y22m4XqgsJWAuLbjLX4g_BKXEQKB> , has had to lay off "28% of its 109-person staff " as the shifting sands of daily deals claims a victim. CEO Jonty Kelt tells Business Insider about the root of the problem, "...the local-offers business, which launched two years ago, was too much work for too little reward. Sourcing local deals is as much work as sourcing national deals, but yields far fewer sales because the offerings are relevent to a much smaller audience." Read more. <http://r20.rs6.net/tn.jsp?e=001i9JdMEOyUSTPVTVZRuiHtkCLxpg3Xk9-atJ6vHWQp956DJQtPRh55x2uWhP8LWqmLdHgCo14ey7Q3gaYq5S8NwPdC-P3Q3CXu6mUrUcGDcKyZynORgbh-868DrHTPegmiDBH7VPBiTIlUQfqwO-jFYUnuKm4lpd0z21LYsLYMTixAsRpOO6g0w==> 


Streamlining Mobile Ad Units


The Interactive Advertising Bureau has partnered with the Mobile Marketing Association on mobile ad guidelines and specs for advertisers and agencies. Read the release <http://r20.rs6.net/tn.jsp?e=001i9JdMEOyUSQxVog3k699h_cad0cPNW5gnC2WZNh40Sw_NTjChHwcXVvwYwP2gLQVaKHcZAbNJHTT16DcYQqzBGlqX-sjKApu1rRxmWokqdcF0ox4dRoJ20HPapN9-Br2> . "We have found that if we can standardize across the marketplace, the ad unit can flow the system unimpeded and be displayed and reported consistently," Michael Becker, managing director for MMA North America told AdAge's John McDermott. Read the rest <http://r20.rs6.net/tn.jsp?e=001i9JdMEOyUSTLrhDYZLYzg37fc4PxMMjm0h1u4nnoPzd_mklTiouCssjtH7Jub_kb0DRefFV7-m9HkOpF0pVbYs1DmFw2sM6UowJGs6ZC7oW0Tc0LrPMaCFxG9h6QjHt3OEHzzQZibnABb2SiWAA63X3xteD11qWdrfBDg4cAPFspFSisDvMln_bDaJ5cHt62beh4Bw2o7ewBNfxazIGbgfwBIfVPPEub> . 


Shared, Owned - And Paid


Traditional ad holding companies have had a tough time adjusting to the rise of "earned media" through social networks like Facebook, Twitter, Instagram, Tumblr and others. But as those properties explore ways of absorbing "paid media" as they develop their respective revenue streams and business models, Spain's ad holding company Havas has created a dedicated unit covering Shared, Owned and Earned media. "To address our clients' need to understand the business impact of networked communications, the SOE partners a fully equipped analytics and engagement planning group alongside the social, content and community specialists," said Richard Notarianni, who will lead the new entity. Read the release <http://r20.rs6.net/tn.jsp?e=001i9JdMEOyUSSEYgozk8KqjdNvdz1xIIRYDzLqq4LTVuSkL5ndhXpZKOyqcLEFHmNNKISDn_6BCJhmSQ_h7Pk0N_oFQIe-5q4da1IfQOQauAHpB30lrsOrvRhzF8TSEFeMtpjsKwzhvCMKY0lBZFf0EZ27voLu7AOHNiaPDun9eslkzLecmLgt_sxTOtZ1oGw7> .

Privacy Fears


It's been a few months since Microsoft set the online ad industry ablaze <http://r20.rs6.net/tn.jsp?e=001i9JdMEOyUSQjqPWqeagdkgJc5-FCZtPMMIzQfDashGt8ov_oneeTQ9MK6KHwo74aLBi3HP4upMKF9fAc_5aX5ZOgXbxOt1EhZu7BViriIOTIfBPexp3SXA3Bb5y0BVSLsDceORz8Epu6zxaj2nrxi-T9Mc5AAW76>  with its decision to make "opting out" of ad targeting the default position of its Internet Explorer browser. Now, the Redmond software giant has presented some justification for its move by surveying over 1,000 online users about their privacy fears. Among the findings, 45 percent of respondents say they have little or no control over their personal digital data and a quarter feel they have no say about what happens with their shared information. Check out the slideshow here <http://r20.rs6.net/tn.jsp?e=001i9JdMEOyUSTT1x-eXEeCjYb0mKJKKiZAwv_Ys7z-LGgKWvd7ZorNxVe5KGetPerdE-VcQDoVjz2BtlqlXQkARQs7oJg6nr_YUGbi1LvZdMWvad_nf_zMsCC3Eq8hL745BKLdsq4yNcuQ-lsMw8c7OzIYIGydW5Skk58oQ0aVnAD2FZ7ud5vIL1D_N-krS785Nlc0vxvmN4QMLgOZCr1hly9Y7_K3XnF4VoMjwtZ7vnE=> . 


When in Rome


...don't do as the Romans do. At least when it comes to Facebook functionality. In a new clarification to developers, the Holy Social Empire says, "You may not use Facebook Platform to promote, or to export user data to, a product or service that replicates a core Facebook product or service without our permission." Advertising partners probably needn't worry as the rules seem aimed at companies that use social graph data to "act like Facebook." More in TechCrunch <http://r20.rs6.net/tn.jsp?e=001i9JdMEOyUSSW6YAG5P84uYR54y8KOeKLNop8mrnKCAyJjvR968vKUQbQQzBOzq-2cL81MlmXJUUhvmRD-3NcPiGMUTKpLDE2dpwF70h8F89KtMNk9Qcif2jex9CQRzLfhaSSkqeeUztRZSsLv7jMjARoJXXDCZ_n-L8i9jeWayJOuDd8SOO0_nQum0mB7ts_>  and InsideFacebook <http://r20.rs6.net/tn.jsp?e=001i9JdMEOyUSTxekU8eKEjpGUxT_J5XSU5SxNABk9IUsTc2vV0rUaIdUb1nhzbLlLAmVRUx3mZaUJ2o_EXo7EkBZXs3QtJZX94J8q9bpCtWcFBDZ-T-J3MzVACD-dmB7dI> . 


VC Data


A visually rich "Year in Review" from VC firm First Round Capital offers some statistical insights such as the distribution of its portfolio CEOs among various colleges (Standford first with 13, followed by UPenn with nine and Harvard with eight). Among FRC's big exits in 2012 were the Bazaarvoice and ExactTarget IPOs, while it made just a few marketing investments during the year, among them Influitive and enterprise social software company SocialWare. Visualize It. <http://r20.rs6.net/tn.jsp?e=001i9JdMEOyUSRhGjVT7U0sMj8CIOG9T_yIYwYstKOH03SveXwWVNMO_fKadE1cbtgwtvrU5lWhT6oYQlzZVfVjoLE1M0MSz92BR4zsthvG3SDnGdCAqDxtMUyW75oXeMYykVEAFyQ_6NI=> 


Ad Tech Fraud


On his Searchblog, Federated chairman John Battelle calls out "'fraud' in the ad tech ecosystem" in a post. He notes that the programmatic industry is rife with bad actors (a recent AdExchanger story <http://r20.rs6.net/tn.jsp?e=001i9JdMEOyUSSCj6Xo0l9aoRrx6ucf059gNZyKgHrNQJTimMlFhzoYYZABWgxPO5es2p_2zLmcd-9k2S2OgpJ4QHkCLZbXS32PDl_q0LiaCPQlSf4dtJ4tIBeKsCOnke8_fD7-R8fOrkaDMEIQ5BO2lOiJnGEgEJxuAOoMIAN3Oy1tSmNY71XB45ccDzB7hQ5MUYBhwvm_bEY=> ). And in response to the idea of an infinite supply of inventory, he writes, "Hogwash. There's only so much time in the day, and only so many pages where actual human beings are really paying attention, and the web (including mobile) is growing at a finite pace. There are even fewer places where marketers can be assured of quality, engagement, and appropriate context. It's time we focus on identifying them, and ridding ourselves of the true source of 'infinite inventory' - fraud." Read it all <http://r20.rs6.net/tn.jsp?e=001i9JdMEOyUSSx_r9ezcjeKk6CXZFduwdCGjmz-qjxfkmESYYaWRZHT8YLq5zPapiTigbaUMjhWNt9f-uZCjBZYi2gmynPYy3vUzu87IxZ-GJOQhbl3xfkDnb6mxCYArQobm11pDgVpXHtEJf0UVfXNvv0UCRbuVMHYynQ4xA1OIfL8bVCpwDWdEQ3_aITY5XucLk0pYtoQRQ=> . 


China's DSP Rise


Programmatic buying methods have been progressing in fits and starts, but 2013 looks to be the year that these tools come into their own. One sign of that is the whopping $20 million funding round raised by Beijing-based demand side platform iPinYou. "We believe that RTB advertising is disruptive to digital advertising," said Ying Zhang, partner of CBC Capital, which led the round. "DSP itself is a viable business model with a strong first mover advantage." Read the release <http://r20.rs6.net/tn.jsp?e=001i9JdMEOyUSSp5IFqwoLkGdPsqty1AGwKtMZOYwx1G_EnO094oWy8Ek_OR1vHQOYxFJKNlFQzzWaJBg130JE42BDRjr2Tj4V3fx2bSRG875K2rCd_t3fcHQpsLzCmV31IqlP37Cvb7nLT8z6tZPZOso3S6MLcH4dQQOO8QsZXn7U6iiSQaRWNag5vBZocFHfQR61q3KIWENR14XqcOrznEqIxd1FkosBdDYIg6Zd1uVjf78-f-84YlisgVNHVIBgX> .

MediaMath Gets Akamai's Ads 

Akamai has sold its ad business, which began with its Acerno purchase in 2008 <http://r20.rs6.net/tn.jsp?e=001cr5ZPaiKnaoNvob1e0pAb1XdhWr-PLyC98OyBholaEyfX3pKqvZVFJdgAtlsVWgJRoNKIWfZ8gGlX9PJweWfdABiKjv2Cb8pfGgcK5cXl15C9stliLJNAHmSAgGulOUCo7aJ5-nEzBgA5aNXJxdMUP5zvSo-9Ntao1z2m6YtUDXF7POfTgTTY8dro4ENQ-jG> , to MediaMath. The deal provides access to Akamai's pixel free technology as the release explains, "MediaMath's clients will gain access to more data for audience (...). Advertisers currently on the Akamai Platform will not have to integrate other pixels for audience and media performance tracking when using MediaMath's TerminalOne [platform]." Read the release. <http://r20.rs6.net/tn.jsp?e=001cr5ZPaiKnap_fMwbZvaIBbF7f5RAry8DRijMZMRxoH22rgQMMmK-C9HR6nkpsk857HHaabksVThfTIatvLv3UTEMAVAdCuXekOg2TOovA0qpxjtVEgbxFWEHcEnjXQxgIZSKdjWJD_7Q0GOy_NsdymwK1c7arNPsloPzDY8litq-hRIWKoWm7wd7WMU6rBDzE5Q-9l-iucybM0gjRF0PLBlcfouTgKlzSoqJsG7m6A5RXplxAule6Q==>  Ad Age's Jason Del Rey says the deal was signficantly less that the $95 million Acerno was bought for. Read more <http://r20.rs6.net/tn.jsp?e=001cr5ZPaiKnaqpk6x2Jkm7ebmLMUdhq-tlr2SFAMR57Nx_b0vOGeKJ5xHmTTt5dLG4LUDNjXsJzEmhARWgnjAINxeve4haqNb6WnjgIiSmMAJKwEQI8phiHCYWJBzbAC1hOa7xKXHBOXbEcwJnWMQMawnzdNN7E4uNCasJz-WilX9aEiGU99LCevWuslj12OYU1WJWMFlMx7RtGG17k1_aUIwnK_N-KWOXj4s5bXvJNECtPs79fTLQsg==> . Akamai gets a seat near, but not on, the MediaMath board.

Adding Ads To Graph Search 

On Search Engine Watch, Acquisio co-Founder Marc Poirier references a little-discussed Bing blog post <http://r20.rs6.net/tn.jsp?e=001cr5ZPaiKnaotJvd7CGRtDpXMlbuV6uQxMC2Xyzd2M70hMOpSkpmtI4CroLfzghjSUwnfBnPS74aTBZu60zWR4EwlwSun24HIycrj4g0_QKrMmoOhubWmFguuzbRw2bFtKt_nJDs3pgQ0HjSccRDpKa0M0AWVjO1TUGXy0pcko5W4bV7VYIZugxkd4KKAEkO-uWlJc8FOZjw=>  and goes over the possibilities of Microsoft Bing paid search ads coming to Facebook. "The ability to use a hybrid of information on searchers from Facebook and Bing combined would mean, perhaps, the most powerful targeting to date. Whether they are anywhere close to enabling something like this remains to be seen, but it would certainly be a game-changer for both advertising networks." Read it. <http://r20.rs6.net/tn.jsp?e=001cr5ZPaiKnar66Fd1eeE5tHHD0DbO13KaUxoCzLYcqEWdBoBy-aDI0PBWZc1Q6obPAzQBnQlVVUvluzF89yJbJ9sAssOMHJlOuv-LXVtenszuVwvhgB3FYrviatEynSXXCX8C0QBdYOkeP0WUS-BGaG7-QJ03PDmxDYfq6u75tI-JAED2JlpKDMGrIA8xQQ7x>  

Managing For Yield 

On the Scout Analytics blog, Scout's Matt Shanahan looks at revenue management in a subscription world. "Revenue management is common practice in the distribution-centric Transaction Economy. The goal is to maximize revenue and profits by pricing products to match customer demand. Revenue management is pervasive in such industries as airlines, hotel rooms, surgery, advertising, retail, media and rental cars. For example..." Read more. <http://r20.rs6.net/tn.jsp?e=001cr5ZPaiKnaoQieoR-v00bm87yeBuPGV9LFrbjvYyazNw5PXhwjQrs993Tz9qcihpFMeq1y6AxFFzBPzE-cwqRIhJLnVw9yDpg58bfRUmJz9ojiI_RXeY38NBd_B5xUkatAb6Lpgu9EGpautbgTqFNgtZVrnMENPu0vFKyCYG34nbMotIfFc6EuGPcedC46pY3Cm7j3YM_EIkO1E5ljA9gYJHcUabAYE6BQ8vz7PRjKuuK2Vyt4B2lg==>  

Addressable? App-solutely 

Russian search giant Yandex has created a new "experimental" app called Wonder <http://r20.rs6.net/tn.jsp?e=001cr5ZPaiKnarU3P35srJPxCQbRXWjBQGnscyj3jmGqhI8_pZvGJrcoPHKwWNyDphZZD0ALVEKqEkNWnpymcgCAhw-KkG9j_PSDrWXuEbvOikFzaL30lO-Eg==>  located in your nearest Apple iTunes store. It recommends stuff using hooks into Facebook, Twitter and the like. Me thinks it could be a nice little grab for creating addressable ad opportunities for Yandex in mobile, too. Read the blog post. <http://r20.rs6.net/tn.jsp?e=001cr5ZPaiKnapOsHE72PkzvxhGjksF5QFiMr-jLYSAqI8yf4vAZHLL5Ft6cxOXPm7__6bY6tTHweklP5RSuYeu9o7nvHUDZLAml-LrzE9oXQ2tP5CIZaPMS8SLy9xFGTUNQmbphA2wgOvA0aso8itKicVij1dFb6ALkgyaLkMxR5w=>  

Retargeting Velocity 

AdRoll says it tripled revenue and staff in 2012, helped along by its involvement in the Facebook Exchange. Since the launch of FBX, the retargeter has managed "over a thousand retargeting campaigns on FBX for 700+ customers." It's now trying to keep the FBX ball rolling with a dynamic ad product, LiquidAds on FBX. AdRoll now employs 120. Press release. <http://r20.rs6.net/tn.jsp?e=001cr5ZPaiKnaqS5f8qEviEJCSdPosQSvG7MH5xhoilyKD62QJassexeclAl1xea8Ja_I8rpXqwWmpcsAVEOLyrLtSqO3fy8jmR0idMTv2DIah-z1nFlMNW5NVfs-vp_gbFY38mkunnEOWFAEc_1iYV4cHy31ETC_UfD6EKoC73PgjixHdlXefPaKGEfwhFQjxG>  And, more in PaidContent. <http://r20.rs6.net/tn.jsp?e=001cr5ZPaiKnapg_7UpNf2w1mGyQ953lYSB8FMKT1vyvNudX7bywgR78bvr79zHmJfQW7jxfEFOVztzfk6VEhn2ZQCNoMrthe2zSjw4CHjUzFF9aj5hg3YLPqzOoUplm1VM81Xoxz-LAr65jGZX6HmwTaulcws0xXO6kxr4tDaNqRgVGU-lbYBmoCv12br50v2kTw8oot0X52gxs-npu98A_mAdzgdpcetQJfRvIMT9LafNM0U2n_CLCA==>

Vox Goes Video Native 


Vox Media, the publisher of online-only sports and techn news sites like SB Nation and The Verge, has shrugged off programmatic <http://r20.rs6.net/tn.jsp?e=001cr5ZPaiKnaoQudkCFAP-vdndp--mQ2GGnRxBj-Vagk8LZiBmsQIGXqhhIENv_lxQC6lIADNHStjoT5WJZvMgwi-hWWNQdhYqdQJCR7cAEFac3QBiC2S8bUJQwXh4bt8psSR52ti0dpkrLI6NL4TubiX5490slez6ng8eo-k_Lk9rfZ2He5JXHFP3RAezETbsKbAA8IHfzzJaazRF4Bzzkoz8g1lfBoTyt0CWr1ESL1vGQszMx7oY_-CypYM7dbnu>  (at least for now), and instead, intended to focus on building up its own in-house marketing apparatus. Adweek's Charlie Warzel focuses on Vox Studios' pre-roll ads on behalf of Ford. "All those assets that enable us to be in the content business-our recipe for telling stories-we're seeing that the brands we work with want those same capabilities," says Vox CEO Jim Bankoff. "They're turning to us increasingly and asking for it. So the same tools we use for our audience, we want to give to the brands." Read more <http://r20.rs6.net/tn.jsp?e=001cr5ZPaiKnarl7Mi23VCm9A_aKbfS4rhaQ1_OKfFln5apzq1iPc7c56JEuO_TFZVodTyIISjqzK2Klv6X9dmwmth7cNiJnkK2y09EHy8VpNaJcB8Bl5J72Z7VIyHwHVZo7-aaU0pIv_zS3yZlq_r2a-05YUN1vPireBbSvBUMlqwWdZoxCEd6Hd58__yB2IyDWmSvWa6Pv-M=> . 

Big Banner's Bust 

AOL introduced its high-def, interactive Project Devil "premium brand" ad units over two years ago, and even at this late date in the "big banner's" existence, Digiday's Josh Sternberg says he's having trouble finding them. Neither can Jason Krebs, the former chief media officer at Tremor Video, who says, "I look at media and a lot of sites, and I don't see them. Ever." Sanjay Jain, the CTO of AOL's Pictela, creator of the Devil/Portrait units, says it's tough to find marketers who can fill the 300x1050-pixel banners, so give it time. Separately, one anonymous source told Sternberg that AOL's frequency caps are to blame for the lack of visibility of the large ads. Read more <http://r20.rs6.net/tn.jsp?e=001cr5ZPaiKnapAlbGD6D1CAsosaPKw_eIcER3BBGnA_5VBglXSgHnZVLsueMUj5gx9CCw0G-KHgEfySsoCTHse693raeybUPht7KGp8AUQxERnVBFcIxCKHl6hHqVZxJMnTHyDmuZ_atvOMeIbApIgmz8LWQQ1tjzhhwhQQmN-P6mM0b6s7W5Gtw==> . 

Seller Beware 

The legions of digital brokers (vendors, sites, networks, etc) looking for ways to "overcome objections" by agency buyers may be needlessly spinning their wheels, says Doug Weaver in a post on The Drift. "The media agency with whom they're all pleading their cases is probably between 30 and 40 percent understaffed. And clients are putting pressure on them to consolidate the number of vendors - to shrink the field of consideration, not expand it." The truth can be painful, Weaver writes, but tackle it head on. If you've got a snowball's chance, wouldn't you rather know that going in? Read more. <http://r20.rs6.net/tn.jsp?e=001cr5ZPaiKnarI30LVkI4Z8AP1KqZCZemd4Qai31cX6K8VeB0nblcejeG1C06b2EYDvw_wL77wA_FlraWkn9a0sEdsiyepgkb4MsZWcljA9oRjIzQyA66lz5Sg04gM51pc>

 News Round-Up <http://ih.constantcontact.com/fs116/1102602719219/img/94.jpg>  

Here's today's AdExchanger news round-up... Want it by email?
Sign-up here <http://r20.rs6.net/tn.jsp?e=001fqmWHzSOpCNmYi4r62HJmbLtIhHKXG2xo7oP4s-EBTbmHb_nKiO6wGLMIK4BTWEHm_7X__nTDSo6kyVP_DLPTj_XHhUXz3jfdUF7JV9YCzHND3_T72nJc68lPjzegxt57gRaFcgOT-A=> .

 

Touchpoint-ilism


With a new platform update, [x+1] is letting customers layer their CRM data over a slew of discrete channels (Facebook, display, email, apps). The key phrase here is "paid/owned integration." From the press release <http://r20.rs6.net/tn.jsp?e=001fqmWHzSOpCO3ViovvpmJzjL5SqP7HYwFjZFX4D_X6ziH09WT4UIaIgrb_KpsJ35tPfwS8w0BHPuGMniQLmeCvwuMZ9lknXPrqkoMdz69h4AfqMFcx2DHi-ny0wL8JJ3N6XbPk5cjI6r10Ezt-fFOyWF_rVrpjcmNA-AiNXYcncR2N9j5oF2gvbov5wVk3pFu1Hp4l7Cxn8xfXCuxSEH_8G37viRxn0v-27BS4SCswIw1dss-EIiTr44Lt8FmzzVt> : "A new data key model...can be used for paid channels such as display, FBX, mobile ads and video, as well a growing number of owned touchpoints including Facebook tabs, email, their company website, call centers, mobile apps, chat and SMS." 


RTB Mindset


On Ad Age, Quantcast's Konrad Feldman ventures into the real-time bidding (RTB) weeds in a piece dissecting RTB benefits and pitfalls. He sees challenges to RTB buyers including - "It demands a mind-set shift from the media-buying community. A CPA-based relationship requires honest and open collaboration between buyers and sellers to set goals that are genuine and achievable. Traditionally, CPM-focused relationships involve the typical posturing, hidden information, and talking at cross-purposes that occur in any zero-sum negotiation, where one side's gain is the other side's loss." Read it. <http://r20.rs6.net/tn.jsp?e=001fqmWHzSOpCNgI9EuSXYX-v69p54d_Ugs9i_n59tD-tRJTffcjjaN7QcfUPIjkSdkrcmYpTiSn2WZHS9ORh3zpwOfFh-P9QEoazpyj6VUJe3RQ3OwmM88qjZX2h5l6XN3klyGOkR1uZjs9X3STQdYVq1fU15ijw3_A9Bzf1S2YhvGRHJC_weyrw9Ee43Q9CJX> 


Search Ad Retargeting


Google provides a bit more color on the new search ad retargeting feature <http://r20.rs6.net/tn.jsp?e=001fqmWHzSOpCNGjLBk-DSYGnt3AvBnYyWlqElKyGR5qIH1t5N-qvHLi9zMOJWmmM20Rgtb3JyC4rK0xjBn2-nIeyT42_N_rhdoemrLZj6p4XVau86ebrei0FngepX10vq-4pq61Kwba5GXHh36bnc17iJHIMRnQp7MefvvQtENR1cSb8FhN9P0nw==>  through the Google Display Network that VivaKi's Audience On Demand unit has been trialing. VivaKi MD Marco Bertozzi had previously <http://r20.rs6.net/tn.jsp?e=001fqmWHzSOpCMBimNmlJGJDr9Qz7hwaXyobPVHjUnDtNzucpQujfV6HLGvB1tig2flSGT950ptJwXBaCkRvBg33-CskJCJYrL-V6qg8pFN3jvn3ZbOUIaF0OEW3aG5-yd3KWr7z3q2Mj4MmJpaxjjE0moPvq3G0waWTvJRNv8YOm3KB0ZA9ISGn35PE0bZ3bLCHHszkrQy3RplkSlHxD64OhA1MOnLI1Yg9d0eVr668HU=>  broken the news on his personal blog. The DoubleClick Search blog explains, "With their search and display campaigns on a unified platform, AOD used search ad clicks as a signal in their client's display campaigns, re-engaging users with display ads across billions of ad impressions available on global ad exchanges via DoubleClick Bid Manager" (formerly Invite Media.) Read more <http://r20.rs6.net/tn.jsp?e=001fqmWHzSOpCOso4VKB01yIZV0hDO8VaZzzA6qkMvmi80XpyIPK5Jxoqr9RQ24b_q5l7i2xQncMBC8vwLnV3e9yId_DezgLtSSUsRxh1fkOYyl3xskKdxGj-9X5W7ncCExfS2KTKEFeZvxqWHVcMLJgPiasIoqxWNaJoe5GMxwHBK2bjvwIqmP3XXqRuRoVpX-S3dA-73GtMg=> . This is a feature ad networks have been selling for a while - the difference appears to be that this is all integrated within the DoubleClick Digital Marketing platform. 


Programmatic Deal


There appears to be a natural disconnect between programmatic buying and direct sales, but Neal Richter, Chief Scientist at the Rubicon Project, offers a solution to more closely link the two in an interview on ExchangeWire. He says, "Rubicon is currently proposing a dealID extension standard within the OpenRTB community. We're thrilled with the feedback and iteration so far. The next step should be an order and inventory packaging API that encompasses RTB and direct integration protocols. We believe these efforts will help the industry move forward in automating premium guaranteed." Read about it <http://r20.rs6.net/tn.jsp?e=001fqmWHzSOpCPdHKq01nz0eAVwgOIWDYQZscnqzPRjKsSLFzKTlhc8sjwKEbtkTLlK5OPdvg99icsiX7jLa71eNNfkOkWjV7un3UakwYZpP4uVdPG-Ep3iYpSkhGF7nhjS10qcd1gikuJpODuwqj0HsXXKSG4iW9I756cBE_-W7RS0aUFlal3dTmvNKwB2CByn0KI-F_t0azvF-JIaBkiOQrydhU4gCnW3xpqyfmoN3MhlXDFsY9OWl__SUte9Bk1n_qddEVnjWNezaSOO-MgkI6I58TB4JPdy> . 


Real-Time Radio


WPP's audience buying unit Xaxis is extending its programmatic arms into online radio ads. The Xaxis Radio product lets advertisers add online and mobile radio buys within their overall digital media campaigns and is part of a wider move by ad targeter eXelate Triton to offer additional placements on online and mobile radio screens and on audio ads (but not terrestrial radio - yet). "Xaxis Radio offers us yet another channel in which to engage audiences for our advertisers, said Xaxis CEO Brian Lesser. "We do this in the context of their overall media plan - providing full visibility and attribution across display, social, online radio and online video advertising." Read the release <http://r20.rs6.net/tn.jsp?e=001fqmWHzSOpCPpIdFXmNf2b4OPIVvgZSrNOCMKkBDB9QzgJH_a8cMLrUgHGbcB6bo2nV7eVyYUWgZM-WaEyGhzM53v0papl3rvfIgSG7UqCTkFqOAaCt3DW9wAia_0BXZtH5r3_VFwjri7AZKfqW9M2xDjbVSXh7GXu9Jy_yKcjGc=> .

It's Email, Stupid


On Digiday, Giselle Abramovich reviews underrated digital marketing tactics. Email is on the minds of several marketers including Michael Beaulieu of Wayfair who says, "While many brands today are enamored by social media and other newer marketing channels, standard email marketing, which has been around for over 20 years, is one of the most effective means of communicating your brand identity and generating sales." Read it. <http://r20.rs6.net/tn.jsp?e=001fqmWHzSOpCPyuIG_jSwJ_oNqLWS76JueNF1rBTmxjRD1bmrqY-U_TlfrDjzhkvtsyjoFbafgT0Col_tWtiMGn_bD-upYQcY1d9IJcnBf14McZ-JyjqO9Ro11E6yNt7pynfnqEFyZR1eiimdQ7oVgniF5IuAnbkijdI9vVtae3vitk30ekJMmKb9upoqr20on> 


Blaming Facebook


It's still early innings for social media, TheStreet's Rocco Pendola says in a piece aimed at Facebook's marketing critics. "Facebook has most of the meaningful data that could actually help determine how well its platform serves clients. No one else has that information. Moreover, there's no such thing as an expert on social media. It's too new. If somebody tries to tell you they're an expert, call them a poser, because that's what they are." Facebook naysayer General Motors is one ostensible target here (though the company is reportedly back in talks with Facebook). More. <http://r20.rs6.net/tn.jsp?e=001fqmWHzSOpCPvN6a61hM4g76w-GHxeq8_dR5djYQQ1AdaZgBWM0NbFDC4rsyRDuPB6-EOnR74NbaTWftnVBbEifoSERLlUgf7rJXFvY1LqxYAHNUdrF9CU7oDlZ2U-pYwQZgu9vOHoauUyeyYofRfhBnnx3NhHMNTIHgOdjYDs-W3xqUGq-Gc4TZG7lUnjhmbQsstjr8Fhn8mx4ABmXF1Og==> 


Unstoppable Display


Pulling from Nielsen's Q3 ad spend report, the Nielsen Wire blog notes unstoppable display ad spend globally. "Display Internet advertising even increased in Western Europe's beleaguered advertising market, rising 9 percent during the first three quarters of 2012. In fact, display advertising was the sole media type to experience spending growth in the region." Read more. <http://r20.rs6.net/tn.jsp?e=001fqmWHzSOpCNa4YyUvsyBBX_EGA3X9fFpVvud3180Mk8Nu5aKcyHYQdihz3rTdOxHtGkZ7UQWw5nteih1M8jqbkjLAr14x1lM5BpFYb2vcPcnHvTGQ7nWQ7J4kcy43BAGzGfXq9pR9poFmUfy4l6LXZJedec-Idf59MzYZa2buHnflT4r_hQlzfTgpCRJp63SON0orBuv-YNAij9iERT2Ni1phvTbDejw>  Has some nice eMarketer-worthy graphics, too. And, get the report (Pay with some PII). <http://r20.rs6.net/tn.jsp?e=001fqmWHzSOpCOvVnccFMvMQ1G-0RoYZkSyq3Napdn5w8KdXTwr-u88p4_8-oRNlzsu7XqAg72bNY8UuN659B53HR3b96YnG8fEzBj135EiY6DNZLYzK_4khmRczRQjXpkM47kYm1Y4QLtlCDwKhNjNE3UT_gGCA8AANeyguX4G1s82XxzaqKGMxtFBAtzeyvHzx1jNN-hOa68dYZZiIXxCq9YQDf6p_VbuMzzN-zB_rzQ=> 


Doing Away With Ads...


Microsoft comms guru Tom Phillips keys off of some commercial-skipping tech introduced by DISH at CES and writes, "This may sound strange coming from a person who works in the digital advertising industry, and I am not taking sides, but I actually think we need to have a serious conversation as an industry about doing away with ads as we know them." Heresy! Read his ideas. <http://r20.rs6.net/tn.jsp?e=001fqmWHzSOpCOglfJBAIhmS9gi2Gdc6Xp9gAK8u7FMQKK2Ij2zQoG7w314O7LR64JDp_VI3b2v4IBRlq1UD4uxLIQrWNQ0QzFpk6Sh64LftSwnbi4UiYMsIV9BZ8znqwzHzVsBIrUxbdS1-PZi1uOcDS8PU6HAx1AOQWuL-EK3-1klMTubchkr1slOdJjQJimJb2i2gT_nm381ePzuwEOfMx6jdHm2A2cqHVxqFqG5u8TvjyWezgz7SuVyTk4t0teKoa3tNIZGER8=> 


FBX: Media Buyer Revenge?


In the early days of Facebook's Marketplace Ads, media planners capitalized first but lost their lead to search marketers, writes Chango's Dax Hamman in a column on Search Engine Land. With the rise of FBX, he says the tables have turned. "The difference with FBX...is that you need to access the inventory through a DSP, or a company that uses DSP technology. We have discussed previously in this column about how a real-time CPM buy seems to scare off the search marketers, and so perhaps FBX is the media buyers revenge?" Read it.  <http://r20.rs6.net/tn.jsp?e=001fqmWHzSOpCMhSTUR5voTOHvUkykdSTpnOyha1G87CWfiiSEtLL6Jqirj6Zeu7ptCdN16vP6mEeECUGxrXzhoY_IDfPjmckympcz5M8tXcaVZuj9EAG3tvZEnGgfUhfzz5ow47CdhhyDWzK3NS9nm4T3yXiFSMyXVGpfRoadwAn4ZypgiKUN9Zg==>

Googling Yahoo


AllThingsD's Kara Swisher hears a rumor that Yahoo COO Henrique De Castro is spearheading a project that is intended to revamp the portal's content distribution and presentation system. Dubbed "Project Zed," it is reportedly intended to make Yahoo the place where people go to find personalized content in a similar way that people use Google for search. "Google will find links for content," an anonymous source tells Swisher. "Yahoo will put the content right there." Read more <http://r20.rs6.net/tn.jsp?e=001fTTRUp3L67MF0mCRFUoc8zCL0ZU0DKtKb03Ecb5rtIxA6Q2zVY5uxubBC3EHWUw1HJvJ2ZtKhx4noQFZgBIM6v2Z5-sf5wE8kdJpz58sABWi0RK4p197GFYYztpAbWzAz22BNInDlphZNwDI8Vm_7W27DR7D8RIbuZrMPyiCpw1t_2ra1TiBGLnAkoe5QOntnMPvFOQR72MxUM_5hc1xmA==> . Yahoo also picked up <http://r20.rs6.net/tn.jsp?e=001fTTRUp3L67MUcr6rxDb1A4x5X9gNlF6_fPhiU5MimlgvjsyJigUu7oap0sMA_HUBDf0CsVHY_GfhQpRbfK_VT6r78ogKT76iae96m030neppxan-j_v0oEDivD2NPxsxoJKqdhJe8SRc-RIRt8mlazxKo_0ysj6nyto-Kg78WtH9LzI-K9QFTeOxd0SFZo-8WAdju8Wt1Ck=>  a company called Snip.it yesterday as Yahoo begins to hoard developer talent. 


Advertising 'Quant'-ified


AdWeek puts a human face to the influx of analytical talent to the marketing business, profiling one-time Wall Street analyst Ben Liang, who took a 30% pay cut to join agency land, and others like him. "They are drawn to advertising not just for the job prospects but also for the creative challenge," says reporter Kristen Brown. There's also the "Wild West" factor. "The horizon is limitless, and the rules are always changing." Read more.  <http://r20.rs6.net/tn.jsp?e=001fTTRUp3L67PI3qCaXqsJYVmdm6u7a6XLtRT-bjIcDsI1X-kwJGOnqsqDciRH3Amaf0-yaJ_6Nhckh-sUPBMXH5d9fcnsvOtP9UjATf1qnDhjmmJJRwahjlHXP2jRZdlTrI3khKglzT7XZq5dreU4M3kLUvf1vTdIvskLdANRYEgSZlYss_BU5V-TsncG7V550Qd76a1xsKeSt5kZTalzqQ==> 


Inkling Of Channels Merging


Former Yahoo and Criteo-an Frank Weishaupt takes part in a Q&A on Boston Business Journal. Weishaupt, currently COO at mobile ad network Jumptap, tells BBJ's Kyle Alspach that his company's deal with WPP Group's 24/7 is a "big" deal: "[24/7 has] big scale on the PC side, and we have big scale on the mobile side, and so we're bringing those two things together. That will give customers the ability to control their messaging across both of those platforms, so they won't have to buy PC from one person and mobile from another." Read it. <http://r20.rs6.net/tn.jsp?e=001fTTRUp3L67Mzh2mLiJm9HZqEFWfeh8azPolj9xKmTraHsF2T9D2-etqbIVHMjXsJUoA3y1I0DjFiQBV9PNq8XPm_kojHY1Trb0sFxbXoEI3uyq-67YbczZzWoRCiYOw3RTumCSP-pCk00Vfl3EgFISxGxoTtO_fjtekAEVK0IhpoUs_Ka9wgw5_LJg-MtFCAPNJ8s-LvceRo4gJdkLrT5RCNao_8gb4f>  How long until the "mobile ad network" is a thing of the past -and it's just a digital network? 


Hulu Gets Ad-Blocked


Little more than a week after losing its CEO, video joint venture Hulu now has to contend with a Google Chrome browser plug-in that blocks ads from the streaming programming site, reports Mashable's Chris Taylor. The free plug-in, No Hulu Ads <http://r20.rs6.net/tn.jsp?e=001fTTRUp3L67MTWdiXzoJ0buq8KLFpuZm0-jJYcMh0xzQeKDVkrM4StgIVprlt_69mxkreRfj7lnQCunsJTbIeX9oSsFYdl0KcKuN1VpeM0BIBXAIjEPP7CafJMM_iIM6rMuJEVvz6gr4TwArKC5_reA1HM6AuJe-S1_ZRbubS-jWr8MWp031HEuO9ZLGHE0MB9Q0yyaiC6FDCoWpsuExwTt6A2uT9HlrM0apLlbbt3IE=> , not only is the first ad blocker to ignore the video site's plea that users disable such tools, "it's also the first extension we've seen to call out an online TV service by name - one that increasingly relies on ad revenue," writes Taylor. Read more <http://r20.rs6.net/tn.jsp?e=001fTTRUp3L67MlzizOYqHh8oB1f4sKjV1_liPLyB4Utw2DUr9jUqAC2TjcKnEKuaj_AwSlOPfKhAN-cpKFj2yVqFBsHxcK2va1ET6d7fqsMfRfgYVZAInKz0t3wg-Xx9EocZbC1shd0V1cpjje5BjY7lXvxEVyzCX4> . 


Publishers' Programmatic Problems


Citing Magna researcher Vincent Letang expectation that 43 percent of display advertising will be bought and sold via exchanges within the next five years, publishers are feeling the pressure to figure programmatic out before it gets any later. As Meredith Levien, CRO of Forbes, cited by Digiday's Brian Morrissey, says: "Even the most successful premium publishers can't go it alone when it comes to delivering individuals, because it's not just individuals marketers want but individuals at scale. So unless you are a portal (and there are only a handful of those by my count), you should be taking ad exchanges as seriously as your ad buyers are." Read the rest <http://r20.rs6.net/tn.jsp?e=001fTTRUp3L67OC5_cZ_liEcNUaLu9VAUlk3b9PeQCxJAk1e0krDWgltp_cZpoSVd1h2UI_GGSSOY2djgto4CzBXS6Ylaa6mZUraw-z6iVhogJuApfXSTrVwSgYA-rlWtKckgi-aI6-96-vfYix3L-1XgDczAzswIxOK8cs_cUlTEo=> .

Measuring The Brand


Analytics firm Moat <http://r20.rs6.net/tn.jsp?e=001fTTRUp3L67MUM-YbesaaGAkl5SkILZGld2bU9aLE7xUKcq7tPyMxRXIhwd11fDnUuWh0YwqdM2K76EKs_ygtnKwKr65m4npVq3dNYe9Jutw=>  is licensing its tech to be provide more robust metrics addressing the efficacy of brand advertising. Glam Media says it will use Moat technology and explains how in a release, "Glam Content Analytics can help determine how much attention a user is paying to a particular piece of branded content and how that attention benchmarks against other campaigns." Read more. <http://r20.rs6.net/tn.jsp?e=001fTTRUp3L67PiwTlf6_6B8TFaYUAdVDZpLZNrEQ0O7BaEODicRlF0dVBtGyiU-unKknvKYWi6vzWJINJcECJ_TFGiuUJPARYW9f6yySRUmiqnYdOOb8izV-EcU-MDiEaY5V2N5YkXVRsbutTmV6UKKmczXV-FdybvvTBwmrSltmqbqNA4hoj4vwHJwGZ1rvW6j7bdVn1wvaFRbPjajV_KB-lFotStTToicRLaWnE1cHAr5OsVjrDPrsvqY9lO84BImisSQNHJxO7VDEvIiSOwOMPWWwHlIHuPU9uusxxvzFe-sIjY2tYo0Q==>

Amazon's Ad Platform


Amazon knows its data trove could make it a major player in digital ads -- either as a data seller, ad network, or even exchange platform. But will it pull the trigger? MIT Technology Review takes up the question, speculating that current retargeting efforts could turn into something more. "Now it has developed an in-house platform for targeting ads to people who have visited and then left Amazon's sites, making it likely that the company will open up these advertising services more widely over the next year." Proof? Sorry, no. More.  <http://r20.rs6.net/tn.jsp?e=001_WW1mcrR30bNO87JMof9qO6yExW8Dm7F8T9EMgXZAIBaTtbYnwV6KY_IaDO9OxYs7lTc5AA2W6NYjA6FPysrknZWgy2BX-wlPWvd9kkwHaVA6fRpjxob9Wqqqd3vm30x28n1GfFf3E9mgCd5pkWqCAwBYfCpAIo-rF2MBM994Bux9ZF040_uNICTHSVz8yK5aK9oLiZ4WCN7FZgHwxdBv7HpWqwfjWlK> 


Tablet Touch


On iMedia Connection, OnSwipe COO Richard Bloom makes the publisher case for optimizing tablet experiences. He writes, "Publishers, like the early film business, need to realize that the tablet isn't just another screen they can post content on. Instead, it is a unique platform that lends itself to specific action -- touch." Read more <http://r20.rs6.net/tn.jsp?e=001_WW1mcrR30a1_TuBjIhlK2tL7V86rUCYbBgvr4BHIqNNm4-VxPQqPWGk6wGirNDL7D0A09R8g6E0rk8sVk_A4IzLMzNsp8JctEualzYoJHbmJPLHvpXAEK6yrxJRwBE1edhrotOX6cSB50VvEs-k_Q==> . 


Real-Time Culture Shift


Traction CEO Adam Kleinberg had some moments to spare as he was watching a stream of Monday's Presidential Inaugural coverage and decided to share some thoughts about the cultural shifts within the ad industry being wrought by real-time. "To say we're becoming technology platforms seems like a misnomer," Kleinberg wrote on a company blog post. "It's a different business model. Not a bad one. Not an unattractive one. But not the same. One of the core values I think we deliver as an agency is objectivity. If we started pushing technology, we'd be in danger of losing objectivity." Read the rest <http://r20.rs6.net/tn.jsp?e=001_WW1mcrR30Zo1TGIv-77wxxqSewGkfqbVfHKMLIzU0ugHD-Dd7HO4DQv5wQPXGmW3HFGnveSPuwxByUFvA8Jx0SlBwUDu_sfW_DkIfraWGj3D4_41fSbyLqMhG8S2-FML2xJ97TQARr0-Qudl_QVR_-Jd0WyH-7tv78L7O2ds6EkxE7zs7M4UEf5SsnEgdIh> . 


Ad Network Founder Fun


Adbrite co-founder Philip Kaplan has launched a new commerce channel for his social network for musicians, Fandalism. TechCrunch reports his company is effectively operating a cheaper way of doing business with iTunes for musicians than other competitive aggregators: Fandalism's cut is lower if not eliminated in certain cases. Let's see ... cheaper access to "premium" (iTunes) inventory? Sounds like another take on the ad network model to me. Read more. <http://r20.rs6.net/tn.jsp?e=001_WW1mcrR30Y7V4WEUTXVqlNP5wmu-J6aTO6mDhpbrvFVel3hR8r4maDvsb7R-G5oUXI2pSi05gCoDGqtL3Rk3hCLdrOQfwesMzCKq3rtpL5Slp3XENgiNwdn0hZzrVimx3_moayp3eqFkjFll37MkbEwKp__7eWpfOIq5hAMmfUQUbwdRVn6eg==>  


Facebook Related


Forbes' Anthony Wing Cosner says that Facebook's "Related Posts" feature in its News Feed may be misleading users. He reference a blog post <http://r20.rs6.net/tn.jsp?e=001_WW1mcrR30awbG_3dUuS7heVI2nDYYZoTFeBIlLE2LeGLYAz-MvrgiiG-4LRAUsEiB5YcCrYxc8gl2HvS0OXTf5Tfym0vyAYVJ0vf2a-yVJWZKFNW_D4kzcJ7Mu-pjVubvvntnHF-svuNIn2GqPgYlErgDxNqrOGPRkiIUQSPY-B4AICuI01cCfey6j2i62XYvKkEzCmrnw=>  by developer Craig Condon and writes, "As Condon suggests, "The only way to prevent re-posted content is to unlike everything." And as Facebook continues to abuse the Like function, or to allow (or at least be unable to prevent) third-parties from abusing it, many users may find themselves doing just that, or ditching Facebook altogether." Read more. <http://r20.rs6.net/tn.jsp?e=001_WW1mcrR30ZpmCPhZYJLhxgPh1hdgO-J_8jM-zH9fDG9Ie3bfYl6vUl5jMerW-nHcNsWlOLE2eejX7jETTW6HOfhD3GvTB7R8M8FzbMCSanxA9Wb_GLQUnmU74hSfhYQBe1ToaixPEjpBKTvN6rPA5zZft_iDbsU4Z8mciPd5QnDh0Urwvn_NmO1GTk4D7TbIadCLOk4ifwE91sytDb-A58C2kTQ8tbt6hWHrMmaJlQkobtytEHSu8RDBWnubNz3qrlP5DJLag0xtBtuzoWn9VW2Ms53QGDW>

Connecting The Atlantic


While The Atlantic Monthly has been the poster child recently for what can go wrong <http://r20.rs6.net/tn.jsp?e=001_WW1mcrR30YULon_i8DHJ7QcCOE5wfF2JsdGyIhdx_JIH8oqs6ZDqrtzYF8BP9YFt6wfHJxUUabioQnlPRzfU-m2YJ_GKOV6FO6vv4vvwGDxmdxhMyqLPPRFLGu9Y1wHf_C29va8X5KiAneqavhG1ylcxu-9xP1Y__pyPcvtYDoIWKBQRXRf98Bvvb7IB4ihzsTKsTQ7gegdR_mPiPNBTDvpBNDlm476NuTRccj6W5aWTSSX5Emf3X59qDY-LVT3DNcJONiz2IbJbwmAV8VFjHTnByX_-e7NTe6yEgG-yx8=>  with native advertising, M. Scott Havens, the media company's president, has his mind on larger digital matters. In a Q&A with Nicole Duhring, assistant web producer for the Washington Business Journal, in response to "what's the No. 1 issue affecting the media industry today?" Havens says, "In my mind, it's the rise of media consumption through 'connected devices' (mobile, smartphone, tablets, etc.); 25 percent of The Atlantic's digital traffic is occurring on these devices, and the technology and business model isn't quite there."  News Round-Up <http://ih.constantcontact.com/fs116/1102602719219/img/94.jpg>  

Here's today's AdExchanger news round-up... Want it by email?
Sign-up here <http://r20.rs6.net/tn.jsp?e=001aFXE16XZ5F2O72_49eU0s1S4kvsdB0aJJ_HjCUYweeGXvY-jB4RL6SO101UwK0jlVUtsRioW-R9MF8TiXVZqVvJQjCPGJwLlr5NlTBB5OLyjQop1pS7qGv4QKG3FUSQJ-rrtKR_YcGY=> .

 

Traffic Tidal Wave


Many publishers still regard programmatic as a threat, but when news breaks fast and a site captures a wealth of traffic, it's impossible for direct sales to keep up to take advantage of it. Case in point this past week: the controversy over Notre Dame star linebacker Manti Te'o that broke <http://r20.rs6.net/tn.jsp?e=001aFXE16XZ5F2_LfyqmElqVhSRBHM3GYxYFkgLPPomh-1pEjNX8mWLDByx6YJ4DF7AGOdn4TrDdBgkt6at9cwAYDR-JfuvK0jZxSVCiKEuIUrm4ZJ_FDwBNLOI9UUF7OVooyWOyVhLQh_GUQ7Oj27wz1Do1V3XBRXpoWb9I66Ktde_BxPmy4MG-1DfVO7D-G76VY5rYgDdWh5HRMd5imUbE4zHjgUkijKcFJaV4OxgRwe2xwgkR4JE9tRnVAqVpFa65QWjpUSR9GEGxx0RLHBiNA==>  on Gawker Media's Deadspin and OWN's Oprah Winfrey interview with disgraced cyclist Lance Armstrong. As AdAge's Jason Delrey notes, Gawker doesn't work with third party ad sales providers (save retargeter Criteo, on past occasions). "Because we don't run any networks or remnant inventory, it's impossible for us to monetize these spikes unless we're already oversold," Gawker Media Chief Advertising Officer Andrew Gorenstein told AdAge, saying that the company was exploring a private exchange. Read the rest <http://r20.rs6.net/tn.jsp?e=001aFXE16XZ5F2O-N97uAmb24fNMlb0061bIeDMwIv4GjwsJaaAX0gpbckZe-qMkCxc2OL4T6j0MG2Cl4hppKpWrP-Cgh22sZnQQRyMSMWufF3vNfgJdz6FMlU0uzFpUQwfdZgP83DZ1-757TjiE0ruyoGrEmU_-kdkIS4E0qtAzbXrwFclbaV5stzcFCA65B73hzg8Cbaj0nvF-pf9S6PR2g==> . 


Havas Streamlines


Havas is retiring its Media Contacts and MPG agency brands, and folding their offices and staffers into a new unit called Havas Media -- which has its counterpart in Havas Creative. It's all about preparing for the omni-channel future, says Dominique Delport, CEO of the new division: "Our aim is to form a new company that lies at the intersection of the traditional international holding groups and the new style of innovative, digital companies." Press release. <http://r20.rs6.net/tn.jsp?e=001aFXE16XZ5F0bLxsJgL2UGQ-tEkykX6felSiN8J1olCV5yejktLfrWWtKh2VQqIeMp6HISlp6UASRA62kQTIcsWe0om6dTBFGBMEkW6MRIWvpnDxhdA1pnXsQYSbo7F1WbIIxdFsNKtGCXliOMSNLIy5vfASskLfeCfU3_r3CTedSW4y9QLtpFuJWmfOi7DgLKfWd8cb4ZMWdmUNSVazN7GHBZQo6CE1exrdYcz6opNTSGhOuFOpqZg==>  And more in Mediapost <http://r20.rs6.net/tn.jsp?e=001aFXE16XZ5F0j7shvotsPAmNNd2zEOcCxNivzig17dl47e2fs0KstbIqDFpciVZsY5NxVLPMy1G9GL26zLZ1U0Anprto6HzrtIH0YiZDYrlOlLlL9wvuzh7xXsVDuQQtM-tIfiJIErodSVEUl4WVWGpgJmJzYnCBpuv2v6RZrdJDqzib8luxuB-xJd-pfcUVnV3Uv8d4pBbbFu7Egu-Uv7WkLldTeDaxc1oSKAsQ2Slkf_95H9Vv4BIqyeqTyWSU6> . 


A Little Less Addressability


The keyword referrals coming from search engines these days are becoming steadily more opaque for publishers as browsers say they are looking to provide privacy protections for their users. Google's Chrome is the latest - read the Google Chrome blog post <http://r20.rs6.net/tn.jsp?e=001aFXE16XZ5F2KqzVFiIpXvMPTM1z2w1i6F5Y3naeHWXhx0WI8bRhxZNlx2RudR9ebEKsjxQmAqpdblLraeCL5ist1jsXdcnW9LUfcAgP7wYtRVrSRJRI_rABpyeFgHzjwEXEqpDaebvmYJE2h6C_43bJur5kubCSmXV2uEqFxOBWrxK0uBp6WS9KdrSWGLnDw> . This is tough for publisher platforms looking to use organic keyword referrals as a way to address audience with display media. Danny Sullivan points out that "not provided" will be the phrase that shows up in analytics programs. Read more on the history of search referral blocking from him on Marketing Land. <http://r20.rs6.net/tn.jsp?e=001aFXE16XZ5F2kP1jmhBfi86_0Z1HyxoolLUkSutBSY1S1d6GEEmJGLqv7-O1Bn5zo_sS7pcgEt_ZjyLcCscxeXeeucNjiEyQ2TVjpAb1ueg2281pvFO7851vj2YTKG33PjB8oJMgoTe1Gz3n0IVleJI2IqmaUUF5C>  


Content Marketing Competition


On TechCrunch, Ryan Lawler reports that video recommendation compnay Taboola is having a "banner year." Wait - no banners yet for Taboola, but it seems that the company is moving to compete with Outbrain, among others, as they'll shift their product to recommend videos and more. Lawler adds that Taboola served "nearly 1.5 billion video recommendations per day by year's end. With all of its growth in video recommendations, the company also grew revenue by more than 750 percent in 2012." Read more. <http://r20.rs6.net/tn.jsp?e=001aFXE16XZ5F0Nt7K6COl1sfO5yl1tn8ICfbfQpf1DpjnE0lwhFNkQv_IPoglNYpFI_uJUtosFiCJAxjrGyrP3aLvB1J1VSKVjiqpUJhl5Q-P7Jx4H5FIoUJn8DccTRkSwRqBxXCaVLaBPKq4ROFNT_LqIfuTS8gxK> 


Addressable CES


Publicis VivaKi MD Marco Bertozzi returns to his personal blog post-CES and offers his observations of the show from an ads perspective. He writes, "So, we have a seamless technology ecosystem developing, let's look on the bright side and suggest that broadcasters do give up their old school methods and let us all do what we want. There will be two implications for the advertising business. The first is that measurement of viewership will become an impossible task without some improvement in the technology tracking it - a big ask. And that leads neatly to the second - addressable TV advertising." Read it all. <http://r20.rs6.net/tn.jsp?e=001aFXE16XZ5F1EOKjEFIeaX-5yLdzkvIwXFGlqA_KaDxHOt-a6MbuKhQWJbvTLytc243v-8gXptlfhVcCJAMLy5dpwrI870r26bobC7A3sGmPcJlPUlda64dSJ6mFlrFYUPF1uMSESz43k81ziK1IcxeW6D7gMHYcciTW-1ld3HkrlsARU9yZOmSE2mvnHMrOWibxcxfevy93aiYM2imCHiAaLs8p48KR55oLpEvX6Ch0=>  Also, get GroupM's CES report on The Makegood. <http://r20.rs6.net/tn.jsp?e=001aFXE16XZ5F1VKnmUOfnCmmgtsBODN_2WPz3xEtSfEWT28KwHo99x0WKn-qaj0YErdJgqS8QQMECCpWPuLdo2auvNX_PCTCiq04YnYXbfe7q3n1HQvfV-YYL9dpDP8kJK-Bi4EsifO5QE5U9Z_Qo3fis007X5iANmVr0_itSWUm53F5fS4ESO1rgBzO_qfQWi>

Social Sign-In Slump


eMarketer aggregates some data on the "Social Sign-In" ... you know, when a website asks you to login with your Facebook ID, for example. From eMarketer: "According to December data from Gigya [...] 47% of US internet users have never logged in to a website or mobile app using social sign-in." Read more <http://r20.rs6.net/tn.jsp?e=001aFXE16XZ5F3uZdcn_eEbKoejajkdZdKcywzY4srx3mg0j4wXTbVZ1erKulYIAgooI-PT70g6ZtqyKPdZT7bPh3U_FN3RWRrAyuEFvHlG2oZLzv6GR-0PSnFe8Sl7qvgqUhOOnOYkDYCkTv-pWr82Wga6gGf4vS2Pjc8LKr8VKo_iMI08HlsauaLWPZXq9YSxzxeSWPRZHeM=> . Beyond the connection to privacy concerns, this should also mean less audience data for the social platforms to target content, ads and commerce.

Samsung Backs OpenX


Ad exchange and publisher ad server OpenX has completed a $22.5 million fifth funding round -- bringing the total investment in the display ad specialist to more than $70 million - with backing from new investor Samsung Venture Investment Corporation, which led the round. OpenX plans to use the proceeds for general growth projects, international expansion and for more acquisitions. Read the release <http://r20.rs6.net/tn.jsp?e=001frvb1vDKCs7RV3_VNPrdxpecOOyquVrv_ZRAC4Ep1HwRzHpmfNBgyG1j2h2IZg5jRVK34Cr83CXBpgwfsX8v26nOmrvDpTl5ERJv2LrfLJgBNaMskP-G2EVI-eqHaN1irfGoSqYjNTpw4WmNUVeekR9cFIpnfJ6OLoyKkeHkHB44B2r3TPH3uDsWonnbsUQeIFUuyuO245ykiW8FVIc1qlsRw2pL-RAjrRzWrSCB91hxnnjEVojESQ==> . Back in April 2012 <http://r20.rs6.net/tn.jsp?e=001frvb1vDKCs7cTJFhDb9HIe4eEmyoecfNPMkhBzZfdCfAvOtLYY-J9EBQBvQK9tXoEme4Un-Rgl6g-uh7tiWOy3NdEJAuzgmZqqRtBi2eE0nYzKG01BJ6Wu7-HFiElrpr5AzRhDIP6GLd9p8BKFn15HiBhrSmiOcW125SESZ1JF18aQQ-wQucwr2WHwoi2h-RY6oNBmnE0FneOYLmgAuqLTj14PmN9oOB3aD5tZY87qrwX-dvZJjTSQ==> , OpenX announced that it was going to help Samsung with a mobile private exchange. 


Serving The RTB Kool-Aid


Search retargeting firm Magnetic's CTO Gus Spathis says on MediaPost that marketers should be impressed by the sheer scale of the auctions taking place in real-time biddable markets. He writes, "In RTB, scale also means having the power to process data at rapid speed. From the time a request comes in, each bidder has 100 milliseconds to respond. In that time, a bidder has to locate the user the impression is for, determine the value of an impression by this user of one or more campaigns..." It's fab. Read more <http://r20.rs6.net/tn.jsp?e=001frvb1vDKCs6mkMTh1bmcqJEAYeMpne-JEPX3cPR4V0Q_01pjHNaE8U7VorjL4u9gBWjWt307s1q3ciUhg-gfi4_fImv-j9U_GOekXxUXQyNlClxS1zM81KNAqC9M1WiTPup8ZsvHugB3msLuo7N-8m2JMCA5wLDAf_cSiM04JGblEgonGvfSNoM4phdyaAgKcPULG246hDdOfm7aCkwkHDcwGNuXXjivo--lCMgYiS4=> . 


Video Ad Targeting Pact


With audience targeting and real-time bidding becoming more necessary for video ads, it's no surprise that video ad platform TubeMogul has started formally collaborating with data management provider Lotame. The deal calls for Lotame's pre-packaged audience segments to be integrated into TubeMogul's video ad buying system. Essentially, advertisers can pick from over 140 Lotame-powered audiences, along with the exact sites and geographic regions where an ad will run. "Accurate, scalable audience targeting is a critical component in successful branding campaigns," says Andy Monfried, CEO at Lotame. "Combined with TubeMogul's proven optimization, our audience data can help marketers put their video ads in front of whoever they choose." Read the release <http://r20.rs6.net/tn.jsp?e=001frvb1vDKCs4r-S2ioF_YX5J8i4M5rHHm5gt9kUJGosSJGywjVDRJ-XFg0RRw8caZW2LpBUera11_Az4YY_srTsTOvsWesS69Wl2HJOHpnt0z86vdKj_7qFp97wBH54qtEqNzPstjizDyldmrie4ljNi1OZP_jK6rQTtz7S2cUQ5es8JY6Bu6QJ1fU9lfvI5uKSrCnk8vJVhldze_TkPjynCQqtaZX2x8kQXGRjSPT2k=> . 


Mobile Money


Celtra is big in Japan. Or wants to be. So the mobile rich media vendor plans to use a $4 million strategic round to accelerate momentum in the region. The money, from SoftBank Capital and others, will also go to hiring new engineers in the U.S. Press release <http://r20.rs6.net/tn.jsp?e=001frvb1vDKCs6Gwk8pwkhAzOt-BjvR9XO0qz2O9qlFsTymOs20YGVNg762w3aIejnfhmjdC6_tcdYnVKSSTWq4BgmpLmXnvhIpdYEwKhxvzbUBRQBZ-eeqhViOM5Ddn7Svy6PrDI4nqhIyLHG5g-gw8q8v_M1wSZ5nQ2q-GjN-HA54FD9C8lJGbShK2PWaHCN_7FmO-kF3KhxQkMYU8g3zZg==> . Celtra says it became profitable in Q3 of last year. 


Let's Productize


Triton Digital announced a new ad exchange for online radio that leverages the partnership they previously announced with eXelate. Press release <http://r20.rs6.net/tn.jsp?e=001frvb1vDKCs69jcEO63o6k05Z5teuZf0skcKy9vEZSH-P87MsbrG07U_vz_REAyl_MDdw8tySS5A4VyoN-h3s3wl5L-5i6BlixmYbAlcpEjIgMHMNad7vaaTmjKgDkmKefobuI_Sn13f3Lm_OvA6lBoyKTD16WEhC> . As you may recall, PaidContent's Jeff John Roberts spoke to Triton COO Mike Agovino last week, who made the case that "letting brands sell to listeners based on their web surfing habits will drive a new wave of automated ad buying and increase the value of the radio ad market." More. <http://r20.rs6.net/tn.jsp?e=001frvb1vDKCs4b--qAvXLrNmZ4gKyWH2G12FBHQZvfnY1T-xzDoa7ljXwGO2yPtEOGSqgYot-7tdEHcGT9inTiasFfcoc6gfCKWVsasQA9V-RpAk9u9ZCj5gE7x5BDRFVNiNFGtqieRofGTXZAhrjZ_kQ6yyDeZqTW6JtjvMGmd0kaABbliP5dtUDgeXLf1Nqn1lkY7M_e00SQjGeHqw-RPDZofPMWCSmx>

The Cuban Missile Crisis Of Ads


Reuters reports that GM and Facebook are "in talks" to have GM return to the paid advertising channel on the social giant. Interim marketing chief Alan Batey tells Reuters, "We're still actively talking to them and looking at opportunities that come our way. I wouldn't tell you that there's a Mexican standoff here. We just didn't see the value in the ads." Oh, the intrigue. Read more <http://r20.rs6.net/tn.jsp?e=0010KJvvgLsLqE3ZMhZBdUHMKemIm7mGImYvzQQdt-Awf7VUt8unSgC0NmfJUXsTIdYda7JYXkw64oQsQF5Ubx4T7jTXXY23apLII_pj5KztyMkzrAh4akv2l-6gpDflyAEXAl2DLKSl96kcXNI7PYEuGLx-VBcT8EW8FB_1XdiwY6TI6oCfoo6btBCRX4LFtsEGX4aR_PvbyN5GyrQDnayxw==> . Will GM put their credit card into FB's self-serve tool - or not?? Tune in next week! 


Mobile RTB Challenge


On Mobile Marketer, Chantal Tode looks at some of the challenges of real-time bidding (RTB) for mobile. Joe Germscheid of agency Carmichael Lynch notes the difficulty of identifying audience: "Some companies are beginning to solve these challenges with geo based ideas such as Wi-Fi connection information, but it is still difficult to verify unique user identity." No cookies doesn't help. Read more. <http://r20.rs6.net/tn.jsp?e=0010KJvvgLsLqElM4eNshDu3wcAn3N6znspGYkO5YLJTnZ_vWVpjYxrb-a7TZSVPIiG5gvVhJ0AhmCqjz8OMpeFLPdj9DstkouNmqIubctleuFlQfpdnlZPQFT3hml4NnNQ3M4HXPhEebypgQsqyyDvs40QXLPs-PpeH-MSPlVXXo4=> 


False Malware Alert


An apparent false Google Chrome warning about malware temporarily blocked access to sites using isocket ad tags. Affected sites included TechCrunch and Inside Facebook. isocket's John Ramey didn't take the false positive lying down and told Search Engine Watch, "So far we have zero indications of malware actually being distributed by our ad server, and zero traces of any breaches to our industry-standard security. Google's malware system is often contradictory and prone to false positives that inappropriately cripple good websites. We are vigorously investigating what the issue may have been and trying to get our publishers back online..." Read more. <http://r20.rs6.net/tn.jsp?e=0010KJvvgLsLqHFwRfd78j8yGLhnF9MlvWNU4qAQBSqcsWqv0IRyYlVY-9p7CuiofjNlPm118GVKvS9pONQ1q47Cofql0NkRQRSEixDF4fpa51pZSpGGa9J0m71S0qNDB6QqtBahOhmamRQ-a7iT_sXZGFTUxshNXxzXNcaPk_Iv8698Tsrc0LLPtBgi0ZYz3ATuaMpHjhmhhr-EG3edycozGo44soLTm-aSWDRH4K9KZY=> 


From Data To Display


Datonics President and CEO Michael Benedek picks up his quill for iMedia Connection and prognosticates on the year ahead. He envisions thusly, "The inevitable continued migration of advertising budgets from search-to-display; Increased demand for data (as we're still in the 2nd or 3rd inning of a long game)..." And, more. <http://r20.rs6.net/tn.jsp?e=0010KJvvgLsLqFjiUWTOGByAO9nuFYG4ESV0DJhtqtNzlNISeD1SYYMMl5KaZrxTmjrFg8qVvKgkGPmqxQGH3zNDNGPvxEsjCtco9BSa9vweyg_t1Yqzj3UB7mJA4KMBOxGWOfY9TtqpF8ADjzNd06WXQxQIOw7w_LyuGl8fOw_LA8rjRNP8VYEBAmghRH5obDiETTXDtepQ--w2wG_zfLo1Q==> 


eBay's Mobile Paradox


EBay CEO John Donahoe called mobile shopping "the new normal" during the company's Q4 earnings call, citing sharp increases in mobile traffic and transactions. More in MarketWatch <http://r20.rs6.net/tn.jsp?e=0010KJvvgLsLqF-9dybBfY9eZQ1Sz0mo0D8ZLy-nDdcfBRZqeQ9GeAX0nkcs4nyeYvPBBTlXDJ61_WMN-RGb22oEn6O5pZ9zcZ_xrpZvY10en7Umwg2U1grVeAJvN0I9YP_udZAGtGHf5Guf-xiQHautbGHCp-DJ-4wzvQiT6-ywLrHW809ssEa3hrFshi3a88T2S2ExYiuhT4=>  and TechCrunch <http://r20.rs6.net/tn.jsp?e=0010KJvvgLsLqGUhuTC9wXtSDqZ7RcKZF592G_FPKvFM-fUXmrQLMAEmYpZUgkl0Pj7XMAO7bQ94jrN-roZoUcNiqp_LkwLNlPOPhXByVE5wnEZ9XSSL-E2iW6j7VVneFE9QCgFbU7OURAA8_gObUh0H2TxyxjnQeid_FeXsDsBwKzJLTtpr4YgsbadJD5My7mwQMVAHuXwCF-sE8qF6EY-aTj1nlfVYtXsLJaiX8rK2E3c1oT1o_c1jwSbqepxtpEOlK4E-0EyaRisUCcPPtyKHA==> . So eBay is officially a mobile media juggernaut -- right? Alas, Devin Wenig, president of global marketplaces, recently told AllThingsD, "We aren't happy with the user experience and we don't need the money...The ads also didn't deliver meaningful revenue. It's not worth it." Revisit that story. <http://r20.rs6.net/tn.jsp?e=0010KJvvgLsLqHE0GumzNH0dJKhKF4gLAV5N0-E0Jw93IzLm2BmQiKXX3UPKr6EksJUqlr2sB38Gen0pyemA3chwimAHjbndZySVb2ynBBmiRpt6tSLo3XLrzMjSNwJAkWa0pOKUVFcZ9DP6x2fyhP2otJJvHStED2EldttYra-mmG3l_cOiiis9E4ra1dsm2NF2i-K4hdNkK3Gefid-zSD9w==>  I wonder how the folks at PayPal Media Network feel about that.

Near Field, Near Term


McKinsey principal David Edelman sees more powerful mobile/local offers right around the corner, supported by Near Field Communication tech. Speaking at yesterday's Adscon <http://r20.rs6.net/tn.jsp?e=0010KJvvgLsLqG4_mZIrRnJFJ1Uy67y1tjEu6VyYg_Agjgpv63JrUScLSNDVGuyCULzu6Mjv2slHCFxAsf8wOhVenYXLHFpytSLThl3r8BxePexgX15xj7IQySC5Z7PLDGhm3GpsH_a98I=>  event hosted by Media6Degrees and NYU, Edelman said, "Our sense is there's going to be breakthroughs in creating more lightweight ways to do this. If someone has an NFC tag in their phone and they tap a beer coaster, they'll gain access to special deals from that brewery, the brewery knows who they are. That's coming in a very close time horizon. Some clients are making plans for that."

Levinsohn Re-emerges


Though he lost out on the job of Yahoo CEO last summer, Ross Levinsohn has landed the chief executive role at newly created Guggenheim Digital Media, the digital arm of private equity firm Guggenheim Partners. The PE firm is the parent of Prometheus Global Media, the publisher of trade mags Billboard, The Hollywood Reporter and Adweek. In the new role, Levinsohn will invest and acquire new digital properties, a role he handled most notably at News Corp.'s Fox Interactive Media, reports AllThingsD's Peter Kafka. Read more <http://r20.rs6.net/tn.jsp?e=001Lb1INK5IMlG2fJ1kbE_jxFuTT-V2kpi9I2GWQ5WRH_9TuhY0y7nKHIvxmuzcOh-5Due3vP4qGEeryCwlFVsSGyzVdmPfj28nPyIV1WLWbatvEzs6b0ImAep2qlO9WBPdcjORxcNdOBQ65ISQF6TjdwJOEx5TvtLTRGDP8SZ6C_HW33SqG43DVp5vlgKVBa-4cOZB9SJ4KVtc1N4P35zg23QH8R5OmeWT> .

Venture capital has dipped back into the punch bowl of performance marketing as Pontiflex announced a $7.7 million investment ($16.5 million total <http://r20.rs6.net/tn.jsp?e=001Lb1INK5IMlG2wWyeMNDvPNs0uvFjKSIdfBZ7Zg-efmoWNW6jiuUwj8bSBWS14eTt3vyiMviZYJI5eDFQ-1u12MS32BgJ2ADRRUWuJK_ZmNh3pfiuDjVDUxbatZseDk4-cVZ6KRJYE_k=>  since it was formed). The company is positioning as "mobile signup ads platform." Read the release. <http://r20.rs6.net/tn.jsp?e=001Lb1INK5IMlHnaRWy6Nr2DjOr8Ej5_C4foXyAgKqvU1n72eTgjsmViil5uaRc851NozIWvmLG0lyZX-W-I2BwKSytwCSa6A-GpcLkK5OIGuu3LIqOE5yti_RELiZL_hh4C0STR0qgsneETWz_3LrIGC5EjGdU3npQ1uBvXT00o4wO4SpWm5wfKF1c9ZXaEx7kFnXw1t-Wih5mNctVi7z39w==>  (Mobile) Data capture, FTW. 


More Graph Search


If Graph Search <http://r20.rs6.net/tn.jsp?e=001Lb1INK5IMlEkXu0l7lCLnZGxXFCTM-8u9NqaBqQgE34n9vGPfYi6Yzt3axL4kffAUx-SwMjSoldGXhgkrLLbJFu_sIr_Z_IrgWqQ4VO6fCGxQxu9XNnM-LkcZWJ1ZakIv2vazAhdPzAz3tjdramD_bt2DACubm1Wk2qBGRzb-_rL79_HpHJytOuttllMMtjBWRNvBPe3GiBcMR-6BW3IjA==>  succeeds, Facebook will one day begin inserting ads into the time honored genre of social business referrals. Others have long been on the hunt for this particular grail. As Erin Griffith writes for Pando Daily, "Social, local recommendations is what Foursquare, for example, has gone after with its relaunch focused on recommendations from your friends. It's what Yelp does already, and what Google+ touts as the benefits of Search Plus Your World. But if any site can gain a foothold in the increasingly crowded arena of social media-influenced search results, Facebook can. Once Facebook teaches us to use it as a utility for local search, we'll begin to use it for non-local searches." Read it. <http://r20.rs6.net/tn.jsp?e=001Lb1INK5IMlG0wF34sYb3IOCTX-k_eo8FDGgYmdaPpvkcm6SF9QF1dMWf5bbOhQNrcXDnACuXGxMLUahvyFmcZKb3SGSx1nFKzbSbTy9WGs_vyGdpJvrTfPel_TJ4S26vTqDpgL0f-xSnXDsbQOOAZPpyUK7jBOrXaTTB-UiJbOpiOuSKUcuOL2lUEGFldOSlt3m8Ch2E46k_5l2BgoepaQV5OH_WSwBGfWuJ4nKb49M=>  More: AdAge <http://r20.rs6.net/tn.jsp?e=001Lb1INK5IMlGUzTWpBv4YdfgNQ9Fnl7FkyNkq4rdD4RYDCW4Rdgse6ykDgwOqY2qN2F1CLtZl0cixV81abD6jARJ0x0HjyMmuxH-Yk8gRqMmwv-r-vu9pLUk6TkOR_2XO0P2k21XH8SicqaiVeE2ZCGjaTMBPrcIuAYAJ_WmbXhk2OJAhbqJ5ar9ozJa3G3ltbVgG-0pKI0ZQrpvVY9uyMa085If5WR_n> , TechCrunch <http://r20.rs6.net/tn.jsp?e=001Lb1INK5IMlHmzNqw9G2c0i9fDhuJOSzStUQHo1TV7grRDLHeYJDqy30lHnKgEEOVsgBjmmf5sCs_tegTZ2qItsMMXN15yXmOXnxrKOOwgfcpwecA6vOp057Ql6IZn0acRB0msPs0SbYTdUi5iGayE6DpwurM1jct> , John Battelle <http://r20.rs6.net/tn.jsp?e=001Lb1INK5IMlH_G8TcqUGkdG5ZyczrDPyx-WksEFtA89Dito4hx0_kDnrArW42_RA1Ls2bitXfC092mwMUn-Qlg2FiEFlAASXvdxl0RTNn9-0speMlOwfrToeYdbddBTy9YoH7TTHFtE3Toiwrfl8bKtfvZbphz4EpHmC3d5D5EwHkOGMZeg4SHDp8XyDTqUkU> . Native Ad Sinks In The Atlantic


Of all the pitfalls you've heard of with regard to native advertising, few match the immediacy of the negative impact suffered by The Atlantic following the brief running of a sponsored post by the Church of Scientology. As the WSJ's Lyneka Little writes, the site pulled the advertorial as reader complaints mounted over the running of a - clearly labeled - sponsored post touting Scientology's "milestones" over the past year. Read it <http://r20.rs6.net/tn.jsp?e=001Lb1INK5IMlEULSqaPDsWjfGnuw8K0v6xsMTtpaxrSH8h0s4JogJmmmZ1Xdc3sHUH8dHsFdofzVsJGTohGxZG9I5Bayav2PYRaPAueQhJpECFl8R7TPTqUU7R8ua_5hchZvtK1yB2JdeCrOVfrV462YHimV1p9yPpZ4_v7xUZUwv9S1cVND1oFsVlPBobwm-SGIQ-L2sL2wyIefxoO3fwBzc6AcPkuT2zzxNpgeRyjcE=> . In the apology on the Atlantic's site, the magazine put it plainly: "We screwed up." Read the rest <http://r20.rs6.net/tn.jsp?e=001Lb1INK5IMlHrysiCd2s4iyohBJp_jtZkDWcXu2e5EItq4Hzdb3hiKPOc4icGZT29XxP-G1kQKnYG_DLYZT3I6f-4WN5adCRda7_FL-DqUmmR67QrjoFg3gyuhoDs-jOrm9dlgDVa1zxsnZ0lWCbAGtATE79LtAphrQGkLV0ra5vSUrDHKiulZAKJTRCIthCNuZo1ASUAZdor-ozc4l_YsrCKYpmsJlFgQtla5vc8VgWUgWojuofJYcH0TXMXnGDtZZPCsTskEON8pB2lLJgbi0kRZ7V5u4X0bT2AmToSXO0=> . 


My (Specific) Space


It's a new year and Specific Media's Myspace is looking to its high-profile backer, pop star Justin Timberlake with its latest site redesign. As The Verge's Amar Toor writes of Myspace's new look, and users (who noticed) can easily reject it: "It's not entirely clear when the site went live to the public, as MySpace has yet to formally announce the launch, but it appears to be a recent development. It should also be noted that users can still switch back to the old MySpace layout by clicking the grey bar at the top of the homepage." Competitive Patenting


The recent mania for technology patents, and the willingness of some companies to sue for infringement, has not spared the digital ad sector. But the era of patent warfare may be ending, or at least settling down a bit. Roger Kay, Endpoint Technologies analyst, tells MarketWatch, "Maybe the high tide has come for that sort of competitive patenting." The story continues, "One effect of the popping of the so-called patent bubble will likely be felt in the market values of companies who hold broad intellectual-property portfolios." More.  <http://r20.rs6.net/tn.jsp?e=001Lb1INK5IMlEdkNQz0l1Vivue_j4YFIsoKG6AxG9fBJJn9DlhP9O0hA0RM-EY5rmG7fDRO8WGD9VberD_Jfl6hJxwnbe7QLYzFoYtj-dJ49YG3l_A0b_pRDi9kdpZAbN8b3C7AHEGM2GH83_62XYQkT7liFcbVcvD-42G3VVnC7X0tJOcL8xpv_C8w6RMOVqrTpRxzBATZKw=>

Mobile Banner Ads


Mopub product marketer Elaine Szu shares some data on rich vs. static mobile CPMs with Adweek's Tim Peterson who writes, "During this past December-the peak of mobile's biggest spending season-rich media mobile ads cost 1.6 times as much as their static counterparts but only returned 1.2 times the clicks." I'd rather be static.
