Crowd Ad


VentureBeat profiles new, crowdsourced video ad company Tongal and its new $15 million funding round.  <http://r20.rs6.net/tn.jsp?e=001tuJhOuNJeYIrWjOCtN5T4W5RleOMmHBPg0iB1ddSngtMNuwCicLmPJjCBuuRCh91d8gDGDufDGsu_bc-BpFQNFR67yFa5xkk9pD7sYqkT89lYDnCAkTjwJJ0SJFb5zDJ_CXAcCCZf6v9YgRxZVLU0f8R2mgqoUnq4Vy9zp3CqAbX80MxGmN1dEuAf8TpCCy03ny-baJy5_o=> Read it. The company, which has been around since 2008, enables brands to tell a crowd of video producers about their "'creative needs' or the kind of advertising they want to do. Tongal then shares that with its community members, who compete to produce the best ad concept. The winning community member gets a cash prize, while the brand gets a potentially high-quality video produced in a short time and at lower cost than a typical ad agency would be able to do." Agency disruptor.


Where's Paparo?


All Things D's Peter Kafka broke the news <http://r20.rs6.net/tn.jsp?e=001tuJhOuNJeYIAVAnWQRUGa16Al_tsR8oL1oOFoWs5bUNNf9LMjTs0WHfDXuHkvCoSCHbIcciwzv7Ez2ySC-mmDsQcOtcqZwSM6GupTIlCAzxEK79M0bnKJBJU63XjwrO6eUaBMe3Wfz4DOWTSbZxZkV3hIaTT6bBnytrTssDSIPNxxT6_NhvGu8G42OAZ1V1i3vdx0p6Z37uVHXaZtpqafA==>  yesterday regarding product reviews company Bazaarvoice's latest hire - former AppNexus product executive Ari Paparo yesterday. According to a release, "Paparo will report to Stephen Collins, CEO, President and CFO, and will be responsible for driving the growth and development of Bazaarvoice's data, media, and advertising products." Read it. <http://r20.rs6.net/tn.jsp?e=001tuJhOuNJeYJ1SrW-u7UGyfdS3_3OGQF4C6_nLC1ECajdfLN5X2cBJDi2hXlwjDFGJ0-vmqi01njDrOQ_slvrNxNOZ6ctsRbQCnF_MRLzRZEyCOTFLegXYiUehNP7wRxlfb3ocZci1jRjO73Vt1_uhVVRRiMGrqUKd8gyl1udAf76Gs23XUTRbtMp93KHQOnU5lqqZrsPcKMVsQWAwAUAwiVOmyBZWCTLshj6RAozVWO1l_YeezQzFvtSypbp-zWo>  Paparo's new title is SVP of Media Products and, specifically, will help guide product strategy which is underpinned by Bazaarvoice's 2012 acquisition of Longboard Media (AdExchanger Q <http://r20.rs6.net/tn.jsp?e=001tuJhOuNJeYKhP90YkAnltur2MLR9CCqahbGfMUesBfbRYAvu7pmAEK51SvWW8RECzFBNcdEjbUm4WTQbVZfKGUJQBUNasrBczRxTVOE4FCw2shmMKxvw7yQTLHfqOE4K979-omtFKMgya45bQRMzGAol4IalJONyAsGK28dqMS19HYQSnrk2qiO0ktsX5bzWDiG23nI4quhwMc5eGVnoFA==> &A from November). Bazaarvoice is currently in the crosshairs of U.S. Department of Justice anti-trust investigation <http://r20.rs6.net/tn.jsp?e=001tuJhOuNJeYIYs0EcLUP-jlSh_qin-M6B1oX5nevELmSQTDHtV5IUHRO-1PZL9lIiawPm4n0bbnjW6d_wNVZUlmXmsDvG56mrrhk2c-1Y_KWQuoOgw_OhsyFKtjdeI_ubhD2xDy4l5EX8D-tAUzazVhfwlfcfusZvG2Y_LDKxlBG5ExzBKlYXNA==> . 


Facebook Attribution Play


kbs+p's Darren Herman reviews the potential benefits of FBX to Facebook as it relates to attribution on his personal blog. He writes, "There are consistently six ads in the right rail, all of which consistently update (and theoretically, drop cookies). Using Ghostery <http://r20.rs6.net/tn.jsp?e=001tuJhOuNJeYLttt1TtDsVuREAPZO50ALJKlJGd6rg-OPpB1Lq1h7YFvyiKO9yt6rLG_Hj6Wtqwl84k_mcImOlwd9Go39SELmeljGeCOaRojy9M5fFTjxeaA==> , I see that DoubleClick has a tag on my Facebook newsfeed as I write this. Is Facebook the new AOL Instant Messenger or Pop Under where it persistently is refreshing cookies all day long and taking credit for conversions?" Read more. <http://r20.rs6.net/tn.jsp?e=001tuJhOuNJeYL64aWYTnx-Mjh6a60qaKhjBPHWo1oO3iSutWhL0LDW8GwvAbRhvNHTTWt8VMCWnldZlp0mtug109Tmofra7slja0-3zwLLevVVBATwHTdyDM0DHbW32cobyNNkJGiwyzhlICn03TxsZRT5s2V_ss13-PpGNLj2WdU775LzAb8ZDYmTQmW8BgTJ> 


And... Convertro's Attribution Play


In other attribution news, Convertro has taken $5 million to ramp up its business. It's a truly global sales push with hires planned in New York City, Asia, Latin America, and EMEA. Says a press release <http://r20.rs6.net/tn.jsp?e=001tuJhOuNJeYI9AcdUHdN4PB1uomjuMhIFsl3X_mXxsx97Ox9EQaGwsjEAPUiEtaJs5CyiS5p4ZZMQRBhpprnKc_acYgF1BNerato5MTnOoAwHStR1WuAyakJ3-VyXVOBj6kt00YCNwgDky1UvUmGYefXJMJ8_8BPFjEVzC7Nwr1dVvW2DMrlXLO-RD0aMTHvRYR0BQrpU_sgG0SIOqz-FhJaFBA5nS3JI3jJQqht7SBo=> : "With Convertro's non-cookie-based tracking, marketers can track and analyze all customer-initiated marketing interactions and touchpoints to fully optimize their marketing mix." The company was rated highly by Forrester for "strong data management" and " reliable account services." 


APAC Men


Demand-side platform MediaMath is redoubling its efforts in APAC and siccing founders Erich Wasserman and Greg Williams on the region. Campaign Asia-Pacific writes, "With [Wasserman's and Willams'] promotion, the agency hopes to build on partnerships it established with Kinected in Australia in early 2012 and with Maxifier in Japan mid-last year. Plans include the launch of an Asia-Pacific office, but when and in which market has yet to be announced. According to Wasserman, markets Mediamath is interested in expanding into include India, China, Indonesia and Korea." Read more. <http://r20.rs6.net/tn.jsp?e=001tuJhOuNJeYJqC35fKPTvRyf4iw6dTiegNvommnoyLy2s8o99onYmkeExhBBa9gmcRmBL8rkfNC6xuM7zGx9DEQ51YaP72f5s4hrQxrVSaGai6r0s9ix9sSzZjc3e81TCEGK5fw9OYTvMr6MNtaRjtxOYeidhrfTHA4qwlbtJ33VzgB8LkmArIYcpSWfHn9XAFSWRzjIVFf9K0VvzDSjw6Q==>

Publishers As Agencies


Univision is the latest media company to add agency-like units within its corporate structure as publishers look to corral budget, provide custom integrations and cut out the middleman. The New York Times' Tanzina Vega writes, "The new unit, Univision Agency, will create promotional content for all Univision properties, including broadcast, radio and digital, and provide research and creative services for internal and external clients." Read it <http://r20.rs6.net/tn.jsp?e=001tuJhOuNJeYLTAHFBVpXrqGagCYszDwz3GfiGKnNGjjf8kIti8C_kgpPbEJJU3ygAX2xoKIIWp6T3EeYNOmh8J3JFAb6Q12AdWSk1zMt2lJ_oVkrO8b7jWH4bqm3iH6CqNsqoDJ5IO7MhTY1m3dI84dRgwDaeN_ecuPr8uyhEHbCxtLkGUFmTz8yhUr64yjiyu8juLchOaTJkUpOFaPCLVtyCXQ234Y4E03AaH6bFeKw=> . Conde Nast and Hearst are among media companies who've made similar maneuvers in the recent past.

 News Round-Up <http://ih.constantcontact.com/fs116/1102602719219/img/94.jpg>

More Than A Banner Ad


On Digiday, Josh Sternberg looks at the New York Times R&D efforts for advertising as it searches for alternatives for the standard display ad unit. Sternberg quotes the NYT's Todd Haskell, group VP of advertising, "This is a way for us to engage with a client where we might use standard banners, but it lets us engage with clients before they go out into programmatic channels, which is something that's strategically important for us. So when we do these kinds of things, this kind of stuff cannot be replaced by an audience extension play versus via some trading desk." Read more <http://r20.rs6.net/tn.jsp?e=001Qfy4u7P6CQ3itDgE3RVP5ZuS2M7xajr1jY1DM0I9PYfZ-9Q9Sy5lN45PEuFaRDJUdT6KacSsekV5LOEMuvuISDL6AmcC8fOOHSbUz5_FtsQkCumACerVF5-ZisWuFw8QePaUak7zAAyLyVbV9SZRz6FXwshtn4bUzgoWLN2LOijeYrMX26kFyK0SrkdHZ1u1> . 


Facebook Ad Differences


Inside Facebook's Brittany Darwell takes a long form look at the differences between Facebook's many ad formats. Among other insights, she notes creative differences from Facebook Exchange ads being delivered on Facebook's right siderail: "Marketplace Ads that aren't bought through the Facebook Exchange can include a call to action, such as a Like button or Use Now button, as well as social context about how many users Like a page or use an app." Read it. <http://r20.rs6.net/tn.jsp?e=001Qfy4u7P6CQ2wkOn-wYj_CGEkmXtxWIhz2oNzm1yo8Vi1WHgI5d05PdWojuhIumM5QESW1q93yOSlo0MDBuQ0Q95x64Bz44dZCXWnZjdIid8Z6kKTo5n43MSbfQ1gN4e3xMRVVtiN8Pc8RC9vm4OXG80seYGgbpcsNd1RJ7SnH5Aw4S_W3rMbPtkzGoU8HXBgsVorBfvut3UeqpJJUb1GSbfuXp7mW1fFqjwu4GZ0GSoFcTawVrPNfwTEZrWLmxTVEiWPVM1BCqJ22GLXY-VSA96fbaMAop9m10AVA689oGk=> 


Mobile Display Needs


Martin Bryant on The Next Web casts a critical eye toward Facebook's mobile display advertising efforts. He writes, "Facebook could benefit from a way of making clear that a certain mobile app isn't relevant. 'Hide this advert' and 'Hide all ads from (x advertiser)' are useful options on the desktop version of Facebook - let's see them in the mobile apps too. Ads are a fact of life and I'm happy to be advertised to, but at least let me fine-tune their relevance." Read more <http://r20.rs6.net/tn.jsp?e=001Qfy4u7P6CQ1PoWbb-b930NErcNOLGm0epk8tEyLaMFJ5ntdGoTTA3BKC5YtMYTH8wuumV2XoHuEU8EOMydZzxSc01cinX82TDXXw6Iy7mDkBW25MEySKuk6xyBq74HGd46VEh6Rwm-kF3DkemheAdchaEIGK4YrDT7n_R6QOdtq91phMxK6lmX6JU42PDT17nEUtsJppdfSZ_MB-wNOFVlSFnR4GJR4UFtTt8im5TbY=> . 


Cereal to Cars


Kellogg's VP Global Media, Betsy Lazar, is heading to Team Detroit, an agency founded to serve one client, Ford. (Press release. <http://r20.rs6.net/tn.jsp?e=001Qfy4u7P6CQ1lj2BjQ6SHIHn5ci1u_rr6-Z5RVCxKTGvqB0uStlX3RuC3tN9VerotSxzOZ_pMmUg68ukfMq4Y0YYBAxiSabGxnI1ZAGxmDdGaO5vkn8wECNdflvc7fwwDXKNO0Fc5Vt66Flu833HnkJMFbf8EA4dY0dp1YKXaKGb0j8w_4UTwVSJ_OVAUXsJyQtO3W1gxK6Q=> ) Both brands are early movers in programmatic media. Coincidence?! It's worth noting Kellogg's audience buying vision has been articulated most clearly by Bob Arnold (AdExchanger columns <http://r20.rs6.net/tn.jsp?e=001Qfy4u7P6CQ2K-MV-OmVly7-4QfEs62Zu1m2dDZWRemtnLKJiAl5qjcHD_z43_1I39SpbT5cki64OJy7nnWo24VVj0CKG_dud7aFlJa55LK83PbCO4v3HdhD6_FFKUYqRm-H78a7EaQQ=> ) -- who is staying put -- not Lazar. 


History Data


Obama overturned an arcane law preventing Netflix from fully participating in the Facebook user experience. The Hill reports, "The Video Privacy Protection Act [of 1988] banned the sharing of any video history information without written consent by the consumer for each video or a warrant from the police." On first glance this may not seem like a big deal for ads, but it lets Netflix push viewing actions into the social graph -- including paid media. Read more. <http://r20.rs6.net/tn.jsp?e=001Qfy4u7P6CQ01qVjhSNuPP_qdlVo7-41-HHjEhtknB1w6Otxus9HKQx9kp4UlAZxzGPmRxPx3eIzfW6FxKnQjNQC_cnmWszBIk9rLiTdkIm5l1suDUW7Z63xcNLE0fFvS_3HGOFAhS4Hq6NTxlyiLTIt1_8MPpie4PdOZRkZWtCiBVdrey_u9daCT65O5ugEm6yp_ZCLmemeDeSmwaL_jMP7D3txS8F_AAwltw0Ch4iCQK9QzX2PZ9g==>

Amazon Juggernaut Update


Dipping into some Bernstein analyst research, The Wall Street Journal profiles Amazon Web Services (AWS) which provides the backbone for many an ad technology company, and in turn, agencies and direct marketers. The WSJ's Miriam Gottfried writes, "To realize its ambition, Amazon plans to borrow from its retail strategy and combat rising competition from companies like Google GOOG -0.20% and Rackspace Hosting RAX +0.06% largely on price. Amazon has cut prices 23 times since it rolled out AWS in 2006." Read more (subscription) <http://r20.rs6.net/tn.jsp?e=001Qfy4u7P6CQ11R8jxIWdowVeeLWJL8Ig0gQdQ_vRK-DbvuIByelGDV7sE9VQb3UMszpDOyTmfuEM2jg-X7Gj5ZMtEUSeZMam4zQmRjcfXOA_Bhol3rkKTaj_DGqaFp5JQ9SOkYQ5pPJZnlcwwE108deQcfNcywSLjW88Pw_Sd8xi53hxULQWi-Mp1ZhUL4lz_> .

 News Round-Up <http://ih.constantcontact.com/fs116/1102602719219/img/94.jpg>  

Here's today's AdExchanger news round-up... Want it by email?
Sign-up here <http://r20.rs6.net/tn.jsp?e=001iozKH4AmczUvDD6vLnAKULKux3oByHbFbYpHFOPMOGT5Eq_CX0oEFZ2FKREV2b-LcHBXizlB4Sh2-HxMrK-Ilv32gAtIMwXrsTS8phq_9cwbGabeFE0-7XJW4v0ic7A19q8-jA1auWU=> .

 

Yahoo's Mayer Underwhelms Agencies

With major ad agency hotshots all converged on Las Vegas for CES this week, Yahoo CEO Marissa Mayer used the opportunity to shore up some relationships to eradicate lingering uncertainty on the part of the chiefs of Madison Ave. Although agency executives didn't get any large plans or blueprints for the future, Adweek's Mike Shields reports, Mayer did provide a clearer glimpse of her priorities. In essence, the word is that more streamlining is to come, something that didn't exactly excite the agencies. "Advertisers don't see the spark any more," said one attendee. "Yahoo is low on the list and not just alphabetically." Read the rest <http://r20.rs6.net/tn.jsp?e=001iozKH4AmczVsSMxSA4ZkXFTynUD1eNd8IVCAa8U6ur0UeA5DbhmCs3UxLN4CUG94IVK8C6iDPluAOg3hkFHsZI4Ox8bEBQrylvnpX_e8mIY596mdfni1YNjUvx2x9WPoWOxPIdcuFs9BW85Ym8JgEnUxPVhVyLJSQtPYL9BPkd_0CL-wYngSebn5Q_SdNcD5c1-Jv1V2yCycCp3kj9te3g==> . 

Sapient Buys 'What If' Media Spend Modeler 

Sapient has bought a company in the media mix modeling/attribution space. Mphasize offers "custom-built, proprietary analytics tools and services [that] help marketing executives make optimal budget allocation and planning decisions." The Connecticut company does offline as well as online channels -- guesstimating ROI for hypothetical combinations of spend across display, search, broadcast, print, and other media. Terms weren't disclosed. Press release. <http://r20.rs6.net/tn.jsp?e=001iozKH4AmczU9M319uJWCvtquek-kGesM1-VL9c5qiGIGvEWPXzP7cElkPDiDcwQMfa2hasfbO1phXdZYTQ21JnWu1mrwg6u2Zf5NVrsPZJ485ekyfMbi83Xnsh4N34Sus7PakApmr-XJ_iWf1LHHvOgJsSraRdn970eLrKSqTVs5ZfCb58F0q8Xwi6b99Ez0>  

Oh, the Humanity 

A blog post from Right Media examines the "human capital" aligning behind programmatic media. It cites a rumored influx of financial industry analysts into the ad biz. "As these so-called 'quants' face the prospect of a fresh professional challenge, their new employers believe they are adding a valuable secret weapon. In short, these quantitative analysts are helping brands determine who their most promising prospects are and that ensure relevant messaging gets to them faster than ever before." Read more.  <http://r20.rs6.net/tn.jsp?e=001iozKH4AmczVWD_SBzfZljw4-svBdl1Fhz4mBz5hrx0rs5PU-Pqls0DM4SJ6EHqzJiYvACsFCeJz6gmWtUD-hx8oI6pIhApU9UnWmdLDiUZKdqLaVuB3xC3Y_p-aHIRk7> 

Triad Media Handoff 

Private equity firm HIG Growth Partners is selling its stake in Triad Retail Media to another investment group run by Dan Gilbert, who also owns the Cleveland Cavaliers basketball team. Terms were undisclosed. Triad develops and manages websites for retailers like Walmart, Toys R Us and CVS. Read the release <http://r20.rs6.net/tn.jsp?e=001iozKH4AmczWfuI33KmnDCVFoFCe9YxhQwhDzWVZPU3Hh6SeLQm_uel4QRPWrIen8jWNTm54w1ZhL7LNtE_n-Hc-xSyP9EdFka0Vya8R44MiYLv5a8wyfS5Tyh64HG-RaB1wP-BGa7Bvi8oQyoh5qXwwFgGqJC6nU6MvyPJ6V8uO_49LhfX9pvg==> . Following the handoff, Triad is looking to expand to Europe and focus on new projects in mobile technologies and social media. "Our next step is to work closely with our new partners to double the company over the next 36 months," said Triad CEO Greg Murtagh to Richard Mullins, a reporter for the company's hometown paper, The Tampa Tribune. Read the rest <http://r20.rs6.net/tn.jsp?e=001iozKH4AmczX1u9wZ7FmM8_9sSkr7x4XMMcytoIRQe9_F7-GO9n7XFmbW3YXR6odBIrf_SIga3aIovNLLGa6L0wpQv8LRwWT3VLflV6dD6KE6nTVz9t5e8zP4KXBiJZPi5zOwLGJ0-U2iY_prd7aee4-z7ngE3d94n33F-XarNZCJmKSZjSs2_yLZaCPmAlgIl6VVgHQHBNlhlMjx7PYG8xDnyPDH509Bv1PgKLjb4I6yWJsSR-8s3w==> . 

Retailigence Raises 

Location-based marketing provider Retailigence Corp has raised $5.7 million in equity for several individual investors. Read the SEC filing <http://r20.rs6.net/tn.jsp?e=001iozKH4AmczUCABxw51OkRkLEFY_jSkGBsc9TuPotQPddaCcuefRyj5i-x9kmL66fHEwTkwYP55kNMZiyhyfrp9FIDB1z8yRVeIMjdt42dql9cOBn53O7PqGiFklapizUXOqcSWJRmoOCy0LvkD6YM6fQUcXKhjSicICUfFVmp4MyyXZWcrA4vvtnVFeuULBYnLWJCBzsxJ4bo_fVpaM2w9TARcjXSVof>  (via San Jose Biz Journal <http://r20.rs6.net/tn.jsp?e=001iozKH4AmczWxh0bdp4wj-5YWsGhliyFBPrBT6om4qt3RLKD9f2_2d1VUl4dQRm1sE11TC8_akV6hK50SDajOCDMa2pvP4u5ncSab-NrB1kJdjCUxys6YkTfBFQW3je9pYLkMHbh6PFPCTc5GMGKz-yyDDYYYvu0QXvGIUmaRZ6QLcA5jJypnp0QVJkysXGCkQqsWtJALRLbtsuAerzyFNw==> ). It's not clear what the company plans to use the proceeds for. Under President Andrew Geiger, Retailigence has spent the past year offering its services to brick and mortar retailers looking for ways of combating the growing use of "showrooming <http://r20.rs6.net/tn.jsp?e=001iozKH4AmczU5-rIq91IIWIgvuayaeIlKGn6uEBvzOBYlFFePjoERXATKdOXr8fHaRAQIfdOOTVSMYVg9w7NxEo_9zs_QObamPm2S9187-X4-QXepIlhSkQYALDkeFCpWIOKuCsFsVh30PFKSOal39FF9_yKx4-x6V2BfBTvANiI=> " by store shoppers searching for cheaper deals on their smartphones.

Anti-Competition And The 'Little Guy' 

"U.S. government files anti-trust lawsuit"... if you thought Google was the target, you thought wrong. Yesterday, the U.S. charged Bazaarvoice with anti-competitive behavior by acquiring Power Reviews for $168.2 million in June - and allegedly monopolizing the social commerce reviews business. Who knew? Read the Department of Justice's release <http://r20.rs6.net/tn.jsp?e=001iozKH4AmczWzH8kLU_FYsJfs0nY9q9KItUANtheNhSDXuMnZotgTTf_P9uZTpQmfFoEmzPtXAcLP_C7MO8NGstlp6YiBp4avnuw1JrYl5yauRq9jPr3YrEdQyXfaTZXPtgGLbSHtjEKbAvIBl9MdvgjPp81OjRzEQ9hq2NBcrKc=> . The Wall Street Journal points out that Bazaarvoice executives had apparently trumpeted their ownership of the "reviews" sector to the DOJ including this: "The company's current chief executive officer wrote that Bazaarvoice had 'literally, no other competitors' beyond PowerReviews." Read more. <http://r20.rs6.net/tn.jsp?e=001iozKH4AmczUuhpVDxmuGzXPy7Hi-d1zMgxBO6s9toNyH0T5tluyUDTLICjTI290VwfxNdTeeJOoNpcoHngJkuNVPsi6_an0sFfT-iuBwLc03Rl7wzGHYbGBimrfqHhuhF9neNzDWmhpnQ1neb58pk0tindbbWh0O26RToH16NOcVKcA0qbbSp-u1R666ncgZ4boza-E7lBkUiTHdCg1K5jFQrIeQj5zLpUyBLtmAFXJrjuYdhCpqew==>  Bazaarvoice scooped up ecommerce media player Longboard Media in November <http://r20.rs6.net/tn.jsp?e=001iozKH4AmczUkeS3QHwmCFm2pUzmXRDUlDFNeT91tuVwWguiXw8VQalHbqdBpiUsqmLxCqMFnzkyGreNfEMnMLp18nPgnKR0Ldhvzl-MttlxlQijrcAFnKVB1_1k8iw5cx86uRik_2Rb9zUJU5BmECrnzr0T8xKXqgohe3jp6m46bxaXCbjiYJXdUwxLnPmeYsyziJORdD01btDb5BUyz4A==>  to presumably monetize the reviews biz and its ecommerce publisher network. 

Buy-Side View 

CEO Jeff Green of buy-side ad tech vendor The Trade Desk tries to make his best case for why Publishers should enter into the world of real-time bidding and programmatic media. His final point is one of survival, "What's the alternative for a publisher? If publishers try to dig in their heels and bypass the need to play on exchanges, don't be surprised when you hear advertisers say, "That's okay. We'll try someone else. There's almost no single publisher that's a must have on my media plan.'" Read more <http://r20.rs6.net/tn.jsp?e=001iozKH4AmczX25FmZUV3p2JWdaRRLu3gEXguGD0SBOkGbDhD-K34X8io3J_TfF34F22u_xsoe-DeqaB-p0JafoLnSFcOgu3KmbWGZjTBAOfQRPguabRW4_Vbk9ygGn3FT60obnKlvJD2mUn8jByreoFax92mZNvZDX1hwnwa6v7z2Nnb0Ra4Vrc5J6voNyzk7UFSMFmFVx1JVR9pQWh2D-V6Q060Qt_krp9jQVZEGKlQ=> .

Listen For The Target

Radio is the "last bastion of context based advertising" eXelate CEO Mark Zagorski tells paidContent's Jeff John Roberts, but Zagorski adds that this will change shortly. Pandora, the online radio streamer, is already selling "interest-based" ads that reflect users' online browsing activity. Roberts quotes Triton Digital COO Mike Agovino who says "letting brands sell to listeners based on their web surfing habits will drive a new wave of automated ad buying and increase the value of the radio ad market." Audience buying saved the radio star <http://r20.rs6.net/tn.jsp?e=001PKr3j3APvOMWW38Uucun9uHc-wucpGn2JpJJ7pQ7ARk6isVbnSdVNfAJ4EW6ONvtQuwFKlSBkLmclbixQ-gIBNWbKuFjQaIN5rOAhBZb_tZat4zHaNEvgoFu2UxtmgoQhncKeYG_QacyjjkSA5G2YuY2DqJr_bG-dSKnTt48KaFHYMUyrC8lUQi94PQPgDl1zEj55T5N7BJUvAxA3SxVcvIpABuDOw2y> . 

QOTS 

On Marketing Land, Danny Sullivan live blogs Salesforce CEO Marc Benioff's interview on the big stage at CES. Benioff may have delivered the Quote Of The Show according to Sullivan's transcription. Benioff: "How are you connected with your customer, your partners, your employees. Email? Those days are over." Read more. <http://r20.rs6.net/tn.jsp?e=001PKr3j3APvOMORFq8Mechj9ezSvEKd8x6Mzom_c-qUTfiF-IhrE_21FEtl8QMnKiPTML4K-Ksyw_jX1Zc7c80obh5TeUb0qrOBLf-M4z7O9X2ilCORdAOZeeaU0vQbIs7L68TFlA6e-ioDBQOdjVEwLpwf-qQx1mjWdiAYGqJGAHsNxnMN8CWyhRjLxci0TOt>  Oof. Marc, now I'm going to take your quote a bit out of context.. but dude, if you don't recognize that email is your ticket into the addressable future, come read AdExchanger a bit more. If email is "over," you just lost your unique online/offline connection that can make messaging - ads or not - relevant AND differentiate Salesforce - let alone all of that sweet attribution potential. And another thing - email as communication is still uniquely powerful <http://r20.rs6.net/tn.jsp?e=001PKr3j3APvONe_BVRCdUXL5EF5qdnNKlRohPw3s41rKixcWeTLkG6q88knwR8otSyUha93sDG25oYIl5agTLLGhQokmcqQkScvA3tO8w2F9IXDLiW5xpmROH4cFGs7GSIJRHHvFJyGnI=> . Here's a thought: put Buddy out front with a paid media program that enables all of your customers to address their email records. Paid, owned, earned - horsepucky! "Paid" is the jet fuel to your company's future. (Let me know if you need anything else, MB.)

He writes, "We believe buying methods will consolidate with programmatic playing a large role, but there will continue to be a strong role for sellers who service 'custom buyers' looking for nonstandard, rich, immersive brand experiences." Preeeeemium. What The Heck? 

Rare Crowds CEO Eric Picard asks the iMedia Connection audience, "What the heck is programmatic?" And he answers, "Programmatic is a superset of exchange, RTB, auction, and other types of automated media buying and selling that have mainly been proven out for remnant ad inventory clearing mechanisms up until today." And, there's much more <http://r20.rs6.net/tn.jsp?e=001PKr3j3APvONYfAO-gPU0m7kLgDMne2yDS_-68nxDmsprEsipRan3CIYdop8MzMX5UX5R8U6q3LDdXJvs0aunlBxbikJ4Kh-lSEVFpOm5MVFYh-5KHIOAG1Q4IxwyC7DGKU4WrPFQGZx1_onLw4OwVg==> . Good riff. 

Dynamic Gift Giving 

Facebook Gifts, the social network's e-commerce feature that was widely rolled out <http://r20.rs6.net/tn.jsp?e=001PKr3j3APvOOO01Vl9PXeyHf6Pgq-eFZmyBrEhHfqxD81enQKI6ZyCBO_BoTpJZ5CcqKpd4Fw57ZXU7EudEomtcudOLKIPSubYOWeUluzSDtTpNYqbnvnq7hh87_HxCBsaZlSdOe7b5haIYlDfPKyuqpVDzlEHpBV3mYvvSfOiVEVgFNtHhtMjMnzWNqjUN-xpVs7h4hR_Jnn6oY-agnNesspBfZHvSR-8EUHfsy8SuCQJoPD5kpmdQ==>  before the holidays, represents the gift that keeps on giving when it comes to clickthroughs, according to retargeting specialist Triggit. In a sideshow, the company tells of an otherwise unidentified "major retailer" that ran two Facebook Exchange campaigns from November to December. The first contained just static ads, while the other featured dynamic, rich media executions. Naturally enough, the dynamic ads "crushed static ads performance yielding 43 percent higher CTRs" with 93 percent of of retargeted ads activated within the first 50 impressions -- compared to just 66 percent of static ads, showing that creativity does go a long way to inspiring gift giving in more ways than one. Download the slideshow here <http://r20.rs6.net/tn.jsp?e=001PKr3j3APvOPeNSj9QLk9ChyIgtL_Mb3_ESUlNAzQ-FUkL-QEBLzTAmYOTeNXvL0WdP3-O-AH1Q3A9D6mYbkjdfJrPEtMmnQ5SfAHIbcVdsZK4yu2CUOsX8yZ20R2KeN5OiBBX3cAm1eYU_BYUOKtuR5xWxUq6vF2> . (Pay with some PII.) 

Cookie Stuffing Meets Johnny Law (J-Law?) 

For perhaps the first time, a legal precedent has been created around the practice of cookie stuffing, or forcing browsers to click on affiliate links unbeknownst to users. Writing on AffiliateFairPlay.com this week, Kellie Stevens describes a gulity plea by alleged cookie stuffer Shawn Hogan to a charge of wire fraud. She concludes online ad fraudsters beware. "If traffic to a merchant's site is tagged through an affiliate link, then the consumer better have actually had the merchant's web site displayed to them. If they haven't seen the merchant's site, then you are committing fraud with all the possible legal consequences." More. <http://r20.rs6.net/tn.jsp?e=001PKr3j3APvOM6gpRgWEAZHbx0n1prqY3MSTvc4EQmod6BUUrdzcL_7Zurt3D9sHOn2aPLfpVfbD64vt9dDEN7Jx9exScsnESMAe5rWfTeHfue2tfBhDy_6S309jrQda-fRMxytAwf9-tJLqHGmQgcrG6LX9uGlc1lLwrdB8OgZtL5bvt6rl6i33TpoDqbscUZBiPKvDGrJ3O6Anr316I1Jj5CHXgPjRY3FZubDOg_yUV4e-7lMj0Wzxkg8Zg626ZiNOTCWVQgne7KS_TgFrNEgw==>  

French Ad Blockade Was Net Neutrality Stunt 

With its move to strip ads from Google sites and other properties last week, French ISP Free was making a statement about infrastructure cost. As Emma Hall reports for AdAge, "The gesture made headlines, spawning a Twitter trend with the hashtag #AdGate, and making a strong case for the ISPs at a time when the French government is negotiating with Google and Amazon over how much they should contribute to the architecture and infrastructure of the internet in France." Read it.  <http://r20.rs6.net/tn.jsp?e=001PKr3j3APvOPsYpiRAWTjQMtUSKtWTs_G_yNUSrD5JfVvbrr79IgVrDIqWaLA5e422ilLy2xQk0ANEfMXsJTjzd3PrvhWMIaU9xU9NShIGExTbTiCGZpTZkzJ0eHQNPCc6zZ_c9po0QGxffWv-w5Ak1vm9ViiYLMHEpulrYiJ8LtRQXTeUcnbEoQW6UIhqoc3Mmt6PiYt7143wC_96AaqSA==> 

Local Ads Boost 

Local ad researcher Borrell Associates says that revenue in the local ad space will rise 31% in 2013 to $24.5 billion as more small and medium-sized businesses shift ad spending to digital from traditional media, Mediapost's Mark Walsh reports. Although the report doesn't have specific numbers for social media-based local ad spending, it's clear that Facebook is driving a great deal of local marketers' digital budgets, as 28% say they plan to buy ads across the site this year. "Facebook ads show little growth in share, running 25% in our Q4 2012 data and the same in our 2011 surveys," noted the study. Read more <http://r20.rs6.net/tn.jsp?e=001PKr3j3APvOOwGVPLgQTzg_cAJYMQ7dPrLOWguO1sXzA9lQbunpoxF08fjSSurav90lRuW_J8T9yCQvwYu9IS_hA1LyhelLNh27m-apAnl1MTscba5CtcixhCw4SndPAz6XsyO1MHtmvfhObGK6KDsHRm5KpLVuAQ2bWxKHBhyYlT5eF3Ry1vwr1vLQPhHjahQHRjobY6gEpAP8zl5xc4pA==> .

Real-Time Games Marketing

Chartboost, which "allows game developers to reach new users through cross-promotion, make money from their games, and collaborate directly with fellow developers," has pocketed $19 million in funding from the likes of Sequoia Capital. Read the release <http://r20.rs6.net/tn.jsp?e=001BARh0q9-qdJMv20nyzm4HakjzB-MGkzmYeLMNTX9bqF7CvQMh-g-EHT-AxwZ8aq4GzkqDViZeTN4NEKg-Q9cAs9yGXOtFZdyp8IWak5u-I2DYGOJ1y7UnyNfOIbZezQ9n_Y6LslX02FqfGwYdRXVwM-MWcOb0U_CN0boNon5QAv8NrvrfxBrHj3mZ-brLWQkoZIQWMtxR4Pou1mCXkGLQbkvYIcIasbdid5eWTG5BCg=> . Last February, CEO Maria Alegre told AdExchanger <http://r20.rs6.net/tn.jsp?e=001BARh0q9-qdLblLk0yxWLsCZ71v53vdzxltlcJlmtjwDQjCzQd0nbXaB5w644-daBdvvOIF-DAwKnYGkablbrxO7D7B_T4MQfbzNbb4jj9wqqKZ7CMXgd5EXJBNRo-XY_M911QzfQ1_DggLdr9HqveA==> , "It's hard to get the developer's app above the noise. To do that, you need to have [our] platform. The thing is, managing distribution power is not that easy, because all these companies are focused on making great games. You also need analytics and manage that in real time."

Native Ads Plow 

On Adweek, Lucia Moses sees native ads starting to plow over creative agencies, "One premium publisher whose site runs a lot of native ads estimated that more than one-third of those campaigns are done in-house or by the client and don't involve a creative agency at all. The publisher, who didn't want to be named because, like others, he wanted to avoid appearing to be dumping on creative shops, nevertheless said his staff can do the work at Web-speed and cheaper than a creative agency." Read more. <http://r20.rs6.net/tn.jsp?e=001BARh0q9-qdJm8TKM0HXANg-4EbkcfqBhH034V3fiQ2YmC3f9GMJ7CoTP-4yd1SFF04qzC8mybwtcqjXNcSxIDsJ-BwTeFdDybjWt0J_59N0ltMrSmE6k-6jaPJ6EqIaBLvgWMr7ZtDdXSxh2kSwMr3rBM0frw2UMEkit9t8EcFKXQtQmYuTDYG3NXb_Q3ipAjDDvp0WbPHtDr-3opIvh0w==>  Barry Lowenthal of agency The Media Kitchen adds, "Publishers know their audience best." 

Offline Strategic Buyers 

Om Malik points out 2013 started with major digital acquisitions by two brands, Avis and Athena Health, that would at first glance seem irrelevant to technology. He expects more of this: "Not only do they need the talent, these traditional corporations need a new technology-centric way of thinking if they need to evolve their business models for the post iPhone world." How could this play out in ad tech? How about more offline ad sellers of all stripes in market for sell-side tech, and major financial, CPG, and other brands sniffing for demand-side products focused on display and video. More. <http://r20.rs6.net/tn.jsp?e=001BARh0q9-qdI7ZAmQSWw673d3ajh5uQO-nVkew8CuRth0roH6hJMFMELfRw-ajyGjFymehxMYj0pGBUL9_usBe1o6uFGu-wu8QAeI4zPZYNBzVjzlXhDYpwUAgnHZ6DHd5qcLWpPzU0v-uCfT6SIux3RO5WPhrEWHRTYJ7CZq1vnDgkiKAxZkSAFLYmuYn6uksJJn5-Pq9wPCoGmn0vL8bQ==>  

Case Study: Facebook Drives Mobile Apps 

Nanigans shared some results from an e-commerce client that used Facebook's "mobile app install ads" to drive extremely high volume over a short, 10-day campaign. The Install Ads format uses social referrals and a strong "install now" call to action. The developer in this case spent $325,000 over 10 days, with some individual days racking up $90,000-plus in ad spend. Total ad impressions? A whopping 32.5 million, with 24,300 new installs acquired. More results.  <http://r20.rs6.net/tn.jsp?e=001BARh0q9-qdKjoQ7_xCcbzV9szDL_HmOBUHCQchqBoPuFQ1P28ltZo-liYXcyI9ZC7VPOwCEzNaJbsxeWqM94BNmpCcM8LDPoHHsZ2zOnVEa3HbmyG_tyzjn5aKfQXDrEzjTmYA5ebkCq1AJDKW4D-aomTeLhwzNk7h0sLMbgzowWNdD_8kUOqGDSsIYAqia5> 

Ad Net Hurdles 

Consumer privacy concerns could delay any hopes of a Facebook ad network, ad agencies tell AdAge's Kate Kaye. "I frankly don't think Facebook has an appreciation for privacy in the space. ... It just isn't their first or second line of thinking," an unidentifed media agency source told AdAge, suggesting that the social network has not joined the Digital Advertising Alliance, the self-regulatory privacy consortium, because "they want to stay flexible in product creation and do not want any outside influence to hamper their efforts." Read more <http://r20.rs6.net/tn.jsp?e=001BARh0q9-qdI4UXox7Ti-_ae9smxrN4ncgEdsRZq_n15_EN2VecEC2bDTl5fxmfSa5hS90aLcGpEv5t91MEztBJRAbKb4I_ONv2UOZAfpbYqvx9jCGrFh5hQAclsDKXekuyZAU_ieprqMepq0IEb4aBPUbpQ2A4eBPO7FWwahDm_WQlWSsElk_zXvsGC7NXkoZG0IiDXm_tOji5U4-ab7jA==> .

Deal Targeting Tech, Talent 

Mobile ad network InMobi has bought British contextual ad provider Overlay Media. The price wasn't disclosed. Techcrunch's Ingrid Lunden writes that the deal was meant to help InMobi's ability to better target users through Overlay's technology and the expertise of its staff. "One of the things that appealed to me about InMobi is that it's more than just serving out ads," Overlay head Ian Anderson said of the decision to sell his company. "There are lots of things that InMobi is trying to do to improve life for the developer. I could see them moving beyond being just a pure ad server." Read the rest <http://r20.rs6.net/tn.jsp?e=001BARh0q9-qdK-gGv-KKm7KTaaxYUqrkGhy_8SceYhx-SefwZ3jzx7c0F4glKmBO5R8rdZX2PohBCGJqLqNR6PKVx-iz8FfLvf_wbGM1nDhAG0caMp6pfSeLIynrGnZ3FFcOgXnRZYexBcVthbU5BhzpK62wliTjCAR3QcS59j8IPeXZKQXsiTc9kTK7RN8D-RZSw8Hp-shrxkOln-OIVa5DPSQzUTVU10RTL-OKPW71RqajDFcNDxCA==> . 

DMP Mo' 

Publisher-side data management platform (DMP) Krux published a press release yesterday on company momentum. No mention on exact revenues but "The company's client base increased by more than 300 percent in 2012 including new distribution partners Centro and Triad Retail Media, as well as new clients such as Apartments.com, CafeMom, Gatehouse Media..." Read more. <http://r20.rs6.net/tn.jsp?e=001BARh0q9-qdI8AJ4JiRLCF0B1i2A-qamlGykrByNAzxURoLEUnGbuNDjzbNl0Qf4MeOAfCPbze70NLO0pEyEVGRZkoKz2hnYgxQGjMQvTX-gesudMh2Mmgd7QY5VoB-dnha7Mn8H8YKl2OxNgtHnNC9ZztuKffDFvWMNt9ZE5Nni0u0Vnt4zTCsS3rG5ChneXVdqTAN27ECo=>  

Programmatic Players 

AdRoll president Adam Berke tries his hand at predictions for the coming year. He thinks programmatic media is coming to four players in particular: "Pinterest and their supply of potentially valuable product-intent data; Twitter and their abundance of inventory better utilized with external bidders (like FB); LinkedIn and their abundance of extremely-unique B2B data and inventory; Amazon has already announced that they'll make their data available via RTB, so it would make sense that their owned and operated ad inventory will follow suit." Read more. <http://r20.rs6.net/tn.jsp?e=001BARh0q9-qdJzDE8pT14-j4XlbXjQL3i2WiAohJ21zivcIjeN2r-ay4WdOw6-lw18O1LF-5sln-FypArFuD9-KfNaJyEARlVZxzVaZ6VRbjT1A3t9J1zTntN3o8aNfjQ6RFfC_LYuqPs=>

RTB Embryo

Satellite TV provider DISH may let advertisers see the analytics on what viewers are watching in real-time - and then hold "last minute" auctions for the ad slots in the hottest shows. DISH SVP Warren Schlichting tells Bloomberg's Alex Sherman the "exchange"-like idea is still in the "embryonic" stage but explains, "The idea is to have certain commercial slots tagged as auctionable. If a show becomes popular with a demographic group, a company could bid against other advertisers for a 30- or 60- second slot. The highest bidder would win the right to air a commercial of its choice." Read more. <http://r20.rs6.net/tn.jsp?e=0014ITIxoyF4EPB85zlqecaH9dsC2fccLCBSJPjc5JBJnN5agaIWvd8RvsgrttpGW2w9HwUF8kJIjFrLBXNjEYVY9ByiL7-XpJPM-FC8zwvyKlgqYZ7eycR8_SXBGGJpWYASozbr2m9Vr17v0kY02omHyzBjriJi56xV3EIzmb8m8SAR3l4_snrVOaKu_nKtkTBSj9McDWj_a10uqRbwQxTk_wxfBH7OOU9>  

French Ad Block Reversal 

We noted yesterday that a French ISP had undertaken to automatically throttle ads across its network, at the router level. Now comes word that the company, Free, has backed down from that stance under pressure from France's digital economy minister, Fleur Pellerin. The New York Times reports, "The company...has long balked at carrying the huge volume of traffic from sites owned by Google without compensation." Pellerin is quoted as saying, "An Internet service provider cannot unilaterally implement such blocking." More.  <http://r20.rs6.net/tn.jsp?e=0014ITIxoyF4EOal9fzVS8gWqURtQd56HSRdQmzezn8tW03hgRIFD1ql0mGNaI7eghMevD84zAS2tusVwhgR5G2jw_DfOPV-EhK3GXKl4tYiwtHdvQc10ddUQVS-J6Fw34QZOdMKqTqWcfnxNijv4ktFP0r2q3ELCSuTJKz9fVR38SFEUzXgIeJNqjVLOMuR-lDIufE_qc-AHdsMEV0HvJTWks4vB4BzZ5aji0LCzvFwKdimiOMIqM_TvYabuWgiiFIEoxbM3O2Z7SuXgYVInr8FuhNDBfNQGrX> 

Mad Hommes To Math Hommes 

The age of programmatic ad sales is still in its relative infancy and as such, the agency business is realizing that the Don Drapers of today need to be as mathematical as they are creative. Adweek's Kristen V. Brown take a look at how the talent needs of the ad business are evolving, as Wall St. analytics specialists move to Madison Ave. "They might perceive [advertising] as not as dry as banking, not as bureaucratic, not as governed by regulatory issues," says Rita Raz, a recruiter at Analytic Recruiting. "An ad agency might be more fun, or perceived as more fun." Read more <http://r20.rs6.net/tn.jsp?e=0014ITIxoyF4EOdfVMjewXYCvNrxQJ-VEYQFZg4eNGnTrohM4GwRgNwGtOsUyYd5NKRwo_QiyrDPiaaTVlutPHNvaeZ7qGG_dzTvj1OYKdNtxnBwBsJAWOtaoz2wQw0RT0s-ceoE_R-Bgoy1u443q-a1o7UAXzg9kK560tTyZaaSp1_tnGKg3n20T9Y7-ubpoJH> . 

Much More For Less? 

Econsultancy's David Moth cites a survey from The Design Industry Voices, which interviewed 500 agency staff and found that 80% said client budgets have been reduced and more than two-thirds (70%) said clients expect more work in pitches for free. Read it <http://r20.rs6.net/tn.jsp?e=0014ITIxoyF4ENj2Jg22k1lSo5yXsEpZScbPfdTt4NnmnZmcD6qbb8DHskWfU25Xp3i1Z8eamgRdW0pcv0dFEfOxp0Up3kwf3GQNbZ9LKM16ovTwUTcjXI-yZ3EFXjLLjtQnn42eRflD7HRS5nVrbtXnTpXdrat-GPhoPyTODekr0FwwFk90SmHbfsWi-vUXAgZ9yytdVm9jmVHosUHkjrnAQ==> . Stef Brown, co-author of the report and MD of On Pointe Marketing, said: "Social media was rife with free pitch examples in 2012, and some agencies are even beginning to name and shame those brands that are asking for free pitches. Times are tough, and it's all too easy to over-deliver in pitch and give too much away, especially when your peers have jumped on that bandwagon." 

IAC's New Study Buddy 

IAC, the operator of such sites as Match.com, The Daily Beast, Ask.com, College Humor and the CityGrid network of local guides, has expanded into education with the purchase of Tutor.com for an undisclosed price. The advertising proposition isn't clear, but Tutor.com is a large buyer of lead gen and display ads. It will certainly have a lot of promotional help from IAC's stable of properties. "Tutor.com has done the hard part, having built over many years an incredible nationwide network of high quality tutors ready to help students improve their learning," said Greg Blatt, CEO of IAC. "We think it's ripe for us to accelerate usage by bringing to bear our consumer Internet expertise in areas like product, marketing and distribution. Read the release <http://r20.rs6.net/tn.jsp?e=0014ITIxoyF4ENS-aIRcyLoAJ8NnkhBNsrxv3R_lQbZT0f6J8xL46kwra36I7Xaki1gSxUglpwWZ0_2b3SRoAWOuQHyQ05qG0s2-AwxjHz3FZ6L5_iTs1ixma-Y8IeQ2seKc_yKZ-zhBetA7V6ji10y3FSNon5AF3NxckYOKnqZ94FREr6bSjhKZM0dT0SWvVLUg3p_Ii6SyF9sA-DDJ9MUfg==> .

Publisher 'Shoulds' 

On the Scout Research blog, Scout's Matt Shanahan delivers his thoughts on what media/publishers should provide their ad customers today. He writes, "A digital media company should be able to answer the following questions for advertisers: What are the correlations between specific media topics and conversions? What types of content (e.g., white papers, evaluation guides, etc.) create more conversions than others? How many audience members are in market at any one time?" Can you do it, Ms. or Mr. Media Warrior? Read more <http://r20.rs6.net/tn.jsp?e=0014ITIxoyF4ENHHmWhA-aK2Eh1im3UQIjomBF-anLEr_k79yE54fGt-gSlL6aVM8MzBsGtE6uJsqhVsiD85hpmEPmzdShsh0p5YTVeLuclmfX1_RZY-UNeh90-Dbzqhk39Eaw5D-nzHB8Y3WZQEY9eAWNsdqlIzGrikLssCoFZO_10PELE7QUSfjxzcdes1gb_gpmrAjN_teGnE5GhKluVWA==> . 

Facebook Mobile Jolt 

Mobile ads on Facebook command a 70% cost premium over desktop ads and contribute 20% of Facebook's overall ad revenue, according to Kenshoo data. (Infographic) <http://r20.rs6.net/tn.jsp?e=0014ITIxoyF4EMmQ_uTYZEJfYYZRo9FgTQSCKEolixwCk1I-Yey2ZiBOXz5AljDPGRk2Jag6xG4haD5IA4TXABQg9HSMmGvAnzDKIWhyj0_a4RupsGtLbuMQOjrOHk61csTfgED6OeSoHUpKco8Bxk06Y8FqWNj1oOX-QSmVBlRDqZ8KDwQ75Mashf0iC5hrKFQIuGiHQhTgFoviq_4jygzPR4MYdjwzOmlwuSwwHwgo-Rjvb7sPbc_fL72SeGLYaWt4uq2hn9w8XK2sOjMdpsVqAl93lJLGkk6>  The finding is based on two million-plus Facebook ad clicks and conversions, but as Inside Facebook's Brittany Darwell noted on Twitter <http://r20.rs6.net/tn.jsp?e=0014ITIxoyF4EMvsbKf3DpoMwCAg3P-q0-tKBXjsjBzLUbQMRO5cOus1ZVcytvcucMDGRA6rDxcSGBNVrNtE0Vz2ZwQnrD0HTBC8Cs4BT6ORYNfU84qcMQ_HjxJ6SGWhG55HL9gHsHbCnaG3ritRpKXv1W99qQ9v8XgPgEqB9aYXEY=> , "Kenshoo data doesn't represent all the desktop ads being created thru FB's own ad tool." 

When Venture 'Bifurcates' 

Thomson Reuters and the National Venture Capital Association (NVCA) announced results of its 2012 survey of the venture capital industry. Investment was up 10% to $20.6 Billion in 2012 over 2011. But, Q4 investments sank a whopping 35%. See the release <http://r20.rs6.net/tn.jsp?e=0014ITIxoyF4EM_fuyirQUY0wlSD1rXWDKv8pudOlPMJeL1YZdjiUjTpr3luVe4IK1TUoiFHcUikiz__FH67h_iVCxe4z_owEnGwcW8H1F3x-8A-2R76oogWr3Z7Xr3Fe6hKPuA_mJb7_v408EI6wZB4u8Gcc3QZ9JdDlfQqq9ZpVJSXidAmooNIAFrK5JD_uh5QxMR-Z-i_88z3sdmBqPmaIrHc5XOjHLYohlvwqvLghQ=> . Mark Heesen, president of NVCA, says,"The venture capital fundraising environment has settled into a 'new normal' which is characterized by a barbell structure of larger funds which are stage and industry agnostic on one end, and smaller, early stage, industry or region specific funds on the other." Foundry Group VC Seth Levine says I-told-you-so on his blog. <http://r20.rs6.net/tn.jsp?e=0014ITIxoyF4EOfz1WXx3bqHJv_Z1Mch4U-y87zEVSu6ivEQIvTZrZswUrJaAka07wNO08FZ42pSKA6fAhQxfpqgwYwooqZ1-zCetVwZOs5Y9U1KD_ETx_CKnsPmlelqMC93auJVZ510t-lquA189a-0MIRRTXnUBnZULPS6OcC36k=>

ESPN's Display Play

With all the talk about "native ads" that resemble a site's editorial content, ESPN is suggesting that maybe making better looking display units is the answer. In a look at its new wallpaper ads, paidContent's Jeff John Roberts talks to Marc Horine, VP of Revenue & Operations for ESPN, about the sports media company's "creative renaissance." The point is to "break through the clutter of the traditional ad experience." Horine also points to ESPN's investment in technology that lets the site display elegant TV-like ads behind a story. Read more <http://r20.rs6.net/tn.jsp?e=001xXuml2YNCiYxZx0aq8ZJj-Bjsl4GrY0965J4B9qHTz64WekhoVD4rEBoACJXedEIaNd6DX0WubzLOrNmlZ2CN5O2kIR4TUNxae9oovSxlFJrPdl8lc0XdwAkV9Lv6fqmD4EYv2HmXA4jvHB8he8MMj1364cDCKzASf0_a3XbUDiTEcOr-RV8uQ-rSluJ_OmhbaLcvAP4tSRDV1KrcPaVf-_rNvjsbCMJxBkL2ohY6aQ=> . 

Changing The Channel 

After more than a year of struggle between Hulu CEO Jason Kilar and the video site's joint venture parents, the chief has decided to step down. CTO Tom Rich is also headed for the exit. In a statement on Hulu's blog <http://r20.rs6.net/tn.jsp?e=001xXuml2YNCiZvgRYz1Mi8IftYURMDOqIc6N_T59dfZuZVRDK0U5GHHpNUQfurjPARSHnkJtfG1uqY_T1dzslBRxenwSlH9Xtpsr0fYM_QgVXsK7mOLf94sgFYXzXAfcNgXIeyQj3C6eR8i7wl70uJ6LaRvLdrFC9y> , Kilar says he's going out on a high note, claiming, "We have proudly generated over $1 Billion for our content partners since we excitedly entered private beta in October 2007." No word on what's next for Kilar, a former Amazon executive, but the NYT's Brian Stelter and Amy Chozick note that he's already been considered candidate for a number of high profile Silicon Valley posts. Read more <http://r20.rs6.net/tn.jsp?e=001xXuml2YNCia4FyfmX0yLZotnzqZpRV5jfdCJ0n06hBLQkqPRdMUbmHhD1aJLvxAGcwNq1lSIVvTatz5vp3MfOnGkcftgKyNFNopmbWhfxp18f1Es6uYY8VmXb63CclaOrXivzpxr43cKrwkPB999u_iA8-ernVXMu3iUJK0qMbH9fJFgc841-aSmMnguKtjHUoPORIqUIbrE1S3XXJnJEA==> . 

Ad Block #Fail 

Major French ISP Free began blocking ads at the router level last week... possibly inadvertently. GigaOm notes, "The update got pushed out on Wednesday, with one of its new features being a beta ad-blocker. And, according to multiple apoplectic sources, the ad-blocker is turned on by default, once the user resets their set-top box." Tempest in a teapot? Some say the ad block feature doesn't work so well. More. <http://r20.rs6.net/tn.jsp?e=001xXuml2YNCiZjz4Zqw4cCNaho-lGR9Kk22vUSC-k7tpcZt5ESBtsSYwWcPLnDKf5odso6MhldfUn4ZobnHJojxyZLaFy62HbAUlMBkUkuiCCPeGaBIKNn_ASkPbMKA5oNaA3MoD7cd62xe2exPBtWgfytReXgdxzTAaXVvOAp661Z9BkQ_GrDMGfL5BnkCJoa1OrqJQjsojp7SRaym7XFsw==>  

Database Matching to Facebook 

Using Facebook's "Custom Audiences," a marketer can match its own customers to the social network's audience for ad targeting. How powerful is this when combined with mobile? Very, writes Optimal CEO Rob Leathern in a Huffington Post column. "The advertiser can upload their hashed email list and create an ad campaign to show to Facebook's mobile newsfeed only, likely in less than an hour. Mobile newsfeed ads have very high response rates, and no longer need to be Sponsored Stories only, as they were initially." More <http://r20.rs6.net/tn.jsp?e=001xXuml2YNCiaukjcJfYvirpTlSrTNZwkj4owP-axArQwy_WGS1QAMgkjDkiKBub0ceyvjHL4EXuny9NcDioh8sOdml59J8S2TAWbxbpR32yiYbEOYNs4bp2oqjyfvfBwqT0tYwT7yoknLzRv_rYvDmNxzE7eNcd-R8EVAdsrUqBqkwdpurgA7dGLgG0bDGp96> .

Video RTB Set To Surge 

Predictions for a strong rise in spending on real-time bidding for video have been coming for much of the past year. TechNavio's analysts have released a particularly bullish forecast the video RTB spending, calling for grow at a CAGR of 55% between last year and 2016. The company essentially believes that the large audience for digital video will finally make an impression on marketers, while the efficiency promised by RTB will result in a shift in terms of how their money is spent. Read the release <http://r20.rs6.net/tn.jsp?e=001xXuml2YNCiYdJaSJ0og68SOV5PNEzsTwZG0AE1R0oPDoCSs2syq0m4eOev25qtiyeYG8KnJOOeWU8Qtac8fOt37ehPO-vCkrSS1iC3kf02AGDHRWcuybOj-EdwAyHwKSAW6SZEa1KBxkqYr6TXOIGM29rDGR_pwetMzXOXTbJtSnZxGBF9IeVA==> .

More Content In Your Search 

On his personal blog, Yieldbot CEO Jonathan Mendez reviews the increasing collection of information (or content) appearing on Google search engine result pages (SERPs). You won't need to go to weather.com to get the weather, you'll just put "NYC weather <http://r20.rs6.net/tn.jsp?e=001xXuml2YNCibH_gLybN-cfuX74XvLcq2D_2jaOYufkFFTeT7uSnqiAAtHRliXD-LJ2N4QZy7pJbTLlWxBw7M1hTT_CsP3-X0MR31silRYNOjw4gC32WAxHwSDqUB5S4kImQLacav7JCkVsDMkwYiZfgMDyhegb2scG54x06kVX3Ae7U9CfNtzzgc8Rqeptuba> " in Google. He thinks this will mean less search engine referral traffic for websites, "Fewer searchers leaving Google and going to other sites mean more people clicking on ads on Google O&O. It means Google takes even more share of digital ad spend - now approaching the value of all of print and half of television." Given his premise, read Mendez' thoughts on succeeding if you're not Google. <http://r20.rs6.net/tn.jsp?e=001xXuml2YNCiZ91NpXlMrh3sqNTboJEJHw6hNxH1Tq2kKCxXhWoMcUCgBS5cQC-5h4wrC49FcxPxhfkAV61EO57GMqkXxJ5QQm9m_dYqtIhEpn4-mrdhvVYYhrhRjsgn1FMxyJuz5EzSRvBNW_xMJ7rGaokv6gWu4cHJCoR82dE7qLSybLaAKfYinMa_ydQS3MrdjylBklCOUay_hGputUXQ==>  

More Developers Designers Needed 

A new case study from Flite makes the case for its platform with client Forbes. The study claims that Forbes SVP of Ad Sales Mark Howard "saw the need for a flexible solution that could empower a team of designers, not developers, to create truly differentiated ad products that command premium ad prices." Read more. <http://r20.rs6.net/tn.jsp?e=001xXuml2YNCib0QHAeESmgDMeJldB2l6sMxNmfi7fBJ-zHTqcbelvrRKHdNEzyZr_-_P9vXYF8SHi5Ds2R629p63GO2Oxs_Qv8yJMr0GhKexGi3yX2rN-G13v0rrOfcH38U2IGhsdiFXVbNokJ2mPufg==>  Flite isn't alone in this area, but it's an interesting trend toward empowering the creatives where tech is their canvas. 

Rev Check 

DataXu co-founder Bruce Journey tells Boston Business Journal that his demand-side platform company had doubled revenue in 2012 to more than $60 million in comparison to 2011. Read more (subscription) <http://r20.rs6.net/tn.jsp?e=001xXuml2YNCiYQxSBrKQ9MF0VeA7EEeHmkRRVTMtphOfJfFreJl--2mZyUBmZyPmMUPdgdL39M0zXQ0rb7SPfeBnU5G5nhxuzuEOUpM3efKkbmrOwTJX81w8HT6mIkw0XwbmJZylkUQQabfdm_45iIEv7NLR70h3-UiUaeG3EHiMa52lDZ2xb-cf1Zxiwp4HVYUTANdokvvME1KjAwp6MHwlyglaiPyFh30jxdXUFf2mU=> . Even if this is mostly media revenue, it's revenue that is no longer going through a traditional ad network and is using exchange-like inventory sources instead.

LOL! Buzzfeed Raises $19M

Social media sharing site Buzzfeed, sometimes cute and trivial, sometimes tart and political, has raised a $19 million third round as it plans to scale up and take greater advantage of its enormous traffic growth. BuzzFeed will use the proceeds of the funding round to nearly double the social ad department to 40 people, Bloomberg's Sarah Frier reports. Ads on BuzzFeed's affiliate sites drive about 30 percent of the company's revenue, according to COO Jon Steinberg. "We see a big opportunity to be the leading social publisher. That's how people are increasingly getting the vast majority of their media." Read more <http://r20.rs6.net/tn.jsp?e=001X0PwJu5A6c-3UvVrczlPg21a_IzRZHqcwlDn9CVQQhna1_Dhw1IQSu1G4eTU93SpgfrI1vz7yvuABTetevKgYZS0WsbaUs8cGp2K6Sr_i2lz8FDbm1qdW82JDaLa5Zs_iqCFv58cZOzEOBcyjwOsUdMJnhKEXgcSxR3DoT4Q0JW1Ce-TVg_YTz5Hfc_YaLuWHPaPEDbKcps=> . 

Election Display 

In Campaigns & Elections magazine, Moat CEO Jonah Goodhart discusses his company's findings about display ad performance over the course of the November U.S. presidential elections. One insight, "President Obama's campaign employed almost 1,400 different creative designs in its display advertising campaign, yet there were some consistent features across many of them. Stylistically, they all refer to Michelle and Barack by their first names. They all had calls-to-action-the vast majority promoted voter registration or asked folks to 'get started' with the campaign effort by collecting contact info and registering with the Obama campaign online." Fun piece. Read more. <http://r20.rs6.net/tn.jsp?e=001X0PwJu5A6c-BgpiuPN58-_qwPsF6vMyDGXZsyeNIdnajzsozKjEMx0v0A7X8lW97FvR6xm3b-f8W8cUtcnm5kf-KqswbyW5g03oNPJuST9plMK4BGy6_jPkHOq-_mLfaVnkfloLbKTVwlzEk52EEG4jlwDTe6FIHEkMrI5eMJQIJjniMRCOzBXg98CUmjSJD0x_hRoan49GZia79CFlwD8Ck-NLQh2bF>  

RTB's Ready For Primetime 

Expect to hear a lot more about the idea <http://r20.rs6.net/tn.jsp?e=001X0PwJu5A6c9TQUlehNl_E8MkbSKkFuIYkNZJFz4b8EcoXZJchnBe862D6wrjDltIu1-KNFerH12-xKbWGyaUlTaGOeq5EwWPiT3ku0GdRfG2DJD8NHIgC7Z04AzCYEV4Zsc39tVu5TZTCH5vO5Xh72dzzP6DRlP4e9EcxcWd1Kux0n28iwk5dlkx3zQ61CXpVoLEr2ytc0A=>  of "programmatic guaranteed" this year. Rubicon Project SVP Jay Sears, writing in AdAge, says that by moving from its original position as a "spot market" -- i.e., strictly "real-time" -- and evolving to include a futures market model, RTB spending could go from $2 billion in annual spending to $9 billion. Eventually, RTB could influence TV upfront budget deals. Why? "Chief revenue officers at top comScore publishers and media heads at leading agencies are amused, and often confused, by the spot market's complexity," Sears says. "They know that the real money is in guaranteed budgets." Read the rest <http://r20.rs6.net/tn.jsp?e=001X0PwJu5A6c_hUdN4aUAVy7h3Baq9HzxLyXWQz_BR8lmsoDx7psOhK9NecYxzbQoLRsdGWcOgj95jKN5nE32wCs2uyTMJi1CFEQfwc82ySLvclZdlmYGp7IVUHOJNe4rKHTu5IQurrOcxwUB7l2BtOc7EIQhkGR1X78g4dFk5fqOINbGB6m4oVy6RdIU5PNLWHdy3mgDmhpqzQk4uG52NZA==> . 

No Antitrust Rap for Google 

Google's antitrust settlement with the Federal Trade Commission is mostly favorable to the company, many outlets reported. Here is Search Engine Land <http://r20.rs6.net/tn.jsp?e=001X0PwJu5A6c8eqLClg6-Ao_m-NM6PcDvzp5GbQvIsgGSc8lkkmKcUxooxksQGbNUDcoEyw1Fu-Tmoad4qoKxJKzrCxfIi-2bZyLP1lNZtIAxNWS-_WC0id58WSr59lNNTNosiRv1Dx-LDNPJmB9j6tVKAvyWJwKzN0joZ5T2QHLoosaaCsIYvxUHQE_tIdLhnnWwGQ47N-9iE5aVHCiwQ6abGFOpuM3eUuYIw8Ii1ESkt9GV52Xxr0auuek0uwsoLevDyEB0fT7UJM88d8l_wG4su1qkJs-mgQX_bQasnk34HPwSfeuWk60QXaQXXmmWhlxwMNCaimLyNPgibObafDPsOUbW-wNZM> : "Google comes away largely unscathed from the process. One can hear the celebrations getting started in Mountain View." Meanwhile Forbes <http://r20.rs6.net/tn.jsp?e=001X0PwJu5A6c95sFSrmsUfi9ZZwzSX4RHhTAQSpgFW2Azf2AAU1Ac8LZaAWrnwlYUnJKnQw8tgYMhCC20eqpbYyKQauRZxXg5X3yRnOEdV07dXQaB5MgJI_RD535mCBZB447iyXgDUge6eAVBscrgftNiszUaOhajoyB-wDITAGft5jta9HWEpw2AtMeUTJt_Bul1jE-fSPh-UhEHqIIRXsbm-_XYRozGMLmsX1bK0NkqKXKUABvOYbu1qMtkA_HOhVLkQZjQRJO4=>  sees folly in the FTC's decision to investigate at all: "It took the FTC 20 months to determine its investigation was largely fruitless. 20 months is nearly a full generation of technology development in the Internet industry." And WSJ (subscription) <http://r20.rs6.net/tn.jsp?e=001X0PwJu5A6c_dHwYn1XI_kh787Bnde9lqz1z-7aFKn_7lkcNLHKnwpDM_Mlv9vQeu6Zpzs0Tr1V0OXIr2IlNxoe34pTkq7LR99Z-BW3LTSIp4A9CAl5VG6YXTs4vwYUbA3OpRSANTmLMeCzQt5jj_R0E3Ml9o4gsh4Bqf2iLhxVax_XKeAnM5ovzzQcpFwKID1wsm2rPj2eTMVaE9D9Ce0ovWkDNl1kCifGZGwitdNw4=>  speculates on the impact for Microsoft: "After being dinged big time for its own practices at the height of its imperial power, the company is now playing the role of underdog in the markets for search, mobile and more. A harsh ruling by the FTC today might have given the company a glimpse of momentum in markets it is clearly struggling to compete in." Read the Official Google blog post mortem, too. <http://r20.rs6.net/tn.jsp?e=001X0PwJu5A6c8I6fwVXV2K_0J9QLLLSXOPtYjKUqslrt1TkTzEGUdR_iHEuQDD38RqhBWwYSloczmbBIqF-33_sjzGKBDj5fMTHfgKqK71Rd_TtohgRpzEFPsAqRPsSwOeZTS8hIUW82CLBy7vFJ3jwhHwQOZLKsSqteRJ_d-D2B0fbGJmQXisYVebB3RAWFuyqivzpg013-k=>  

Yielding For Ads & More 

On his company blog, Krux CEO Tom Chavez delivers observations on 2013. Among them the progressive move toward a more holistic look at yield which isn't ads alone. He writes, "2013 will be the year we take critical early paces beyond ads into content and commerce. While data connectivity outside the realm of ads will need a little time to take root, its early proof points will most certainly occur in 2013, setting the stage for much greater uptick in 2014 and 2015." Read more. <http://r20.rs6.net/tn.jsp?e=001X0PwJu5A6c9S5a0qs6PS0nWAegmCO-kyUEHjKzYgeyCCXZdh7SbQJwL2VdiIXJsGNnCRU4dL-DWv5wyDTNEXVgt7shDb207CDe0z_q9dOrircDLGCF8gRQfPi-BGxHIPv115H2QwcXBH-so0-w2u3GusZ2NoLVIzRzV5_gYIeqrbpoWP4J7czdh5hDHTcYXS>

Partner Flow 

SocialFlow is the latest social marketing player to be given membership in Facebook's Preferred Marketing Developers (PMD) program. The company's Crescendo product, billed as an "Attention Buying Platform," will allow it to better connect its clients to Facebook's members. Missy Godfrey, CEO, SocialFlow said, "Our inclusion in the PMD program underscores our commitment to helping clients optimize their ad targeting and creative in real time. We are proud to be part of this Facebook program that helps developers create products to improve the ease of use and effectiveness of social marketing." Read the release <http://r20.rs6.net/tn.jsp?e=001X0PwJu5A6c8kW3qOJhucOW-hyoLU4QjcwljrzTzApu_nc9SlFw-gjNenhx-79W6mDt-ejvnhbb22rtTU1CsCGOyyrKIG478uONkxdIwelTCxKG0EfkJ_FG-trAqumCOUrhdfwBviXWTFgm-PklwFrE9HZepFJ2uXi1BUOMDV_2QMLrGf2hOdi1PncsD_QBmLNxogoe4Q6jGHKH_RO-B_esBiPNvdDiGc> . 

FBX DSP Feedback 

CEO Joe Zawadzki of demand-side platform MediaMath joined the talking heads on Bloomberg TV on Monday to discuss Facebook, its ad exchange and MediaMath's offering. Zawadzki tells the interviewer, "The performance metrics are there. We've got hundreds of advertisers that are running on the Facebook Exchange and north of 90% of advertisers are seeing A) great performance and B) doing it at meaningful scale." See Zawadzki in action. <http://r20.rs6.net/tn.jsp?e=001X0PwJu5A6c9W1Fk4Aknst6GIBUm7g6E3XxpT4WVpxFurMs4HY7hD9q_KQcmDp4NvpMFVyLwIPSMP1p3joHB2jOjtm5JBlBlTDQGC1H1xN5JpNjCQfIR8YJiRhWiWkYQlyRXHIPQN9dRE-gv9iGpUsWa5t60BI1mwZ-PrxJF78agSjelMW0YFN2QltnC0aCQp>  FBX remains the "cool kids" exchange. 

The Google Panel 

Google has taken steps to prop up its little-known online consumer panel, called Screenwise. With adoption reportedly stalling, Google began offering cash payments to some households. The New York Times reports on one. "With so many devices in her family, Google was offering to pay about $100 a month. That was tempting, but Carolyn had some privacy qualms." Read the qualms <http://r20.rs6.net/tn.jsp?e=001X0PwJu5A6c-R3d20cfa7QpgkX9BEkXL0g4FVdF56cWqqK-0n2RLEyFnNH4YPFoOurRbWpKRzMlo-hC_RwEmQrMeI61O_STCi4Re5CUu6W0WeomfVx610rAZmxG1f2tcDk-ytZi1SSMrDpPzlfIduflMScWJvC660NAylbSZy5_0Z2iLM02QvCNJ86T9etJMiXvDlTo0PfB4gWeTU_1XxSg==> .

Piracy And Ad Networks 

The University of Southern California (USC) Annenberg Innovation Lab released a new study yesterday which claims that ad networks are continuing to support piracy of digitized content. OpenX, Google, Yahoo (including Right Media), Quantcast and Infolinks are listed among the top 10 providers of advertising to sites with pirated content says USC Annenberg. The lab promises that the top 10 advertising brands will be out-ed in the "coming months." Read more (PDF) <http://r20.rs6.net/tn.jsp?e=001VjdUGZ86zYrYYKhmRUs1WnuFHC9aBQvcDEBG7QPr9V8DHo1fd3V48BWg4mZ3-q4DlzilXayzAIDFDfClJa8uVm5LJdAeEQHQYGuR4WIfoQ_hTz9r4-BmhuEP1d9R2mOfneXCy2IpD54UIzoQwuemk1TlsA0XZe-Nyr3PKGutUnk3jm1od4P_3Mo9sGkl7xRC> . Google responded in a Marketing Land article saying in part, "We have not seen a copy of this report and don't know the methodology, but to the extent it suggests that Google ads are a major source of funds for major pirate sites, we believe it is mistaken...." Read more. <http://r20.rs6.net/tn.jsp?e=001VjdUGZ86zYrHzwNuIQqLmgaxiBuh7CBWk2dBx-RzF8NYpef-C6Aun3yoYubxnRKp8P9QynG54oI461J3zlb8JqdZ81IKpgBK1-aVY3KyGrmMSsc5O-hKwTeyBuG_4v_64jpZ9NE2mLbEDinSxgIf1QSIUYqd0ZVfLIH9JmScUU3VVVRjGELoaOk-hCx1gbdtTAK9JzFXH4aY7oF4Eu6Scj_a9Kiz8sv6>  

COPPA And Ad Networks 

Did you hear? The FTC recently amended the COPPA children's privacy rule. Among the changes is a new explicit reference to website plugins and ad networks. In a blog post for the FTC, agency CTO Steve Bellovin writes, "The definition of a website...directed to children is expanded to include plug-ins or ad networks that have actual knowledge that they are collecting personal information through a child-directed website or online service." But what if you're not collecting data that would be classified as "personal" under COPPA? Then you needn't fret. More.  <http://r20.rs6.net/tn.jsp?e=001VjdUGZ86zYpkD0gPyvOw2OlJuhgRX7-BYVh6KIMpMHq8BHVmMYUoM8GeXcld6a5cItMKlNHD3uAZy1lWMg7L5TXZrYrmqqehREkxi0pJ414jCGLUKn_lR1j8lbuaiHnVWqAmJoVqpLkbEk6q_SeGKDi5Exvou-zfE2m1Z-hiytvSxKgW4e_ivQ==> 

Privacy Grunt Work 

The decision by some publishers -- most notably Facebook and Amazon -- not to join the industry's "Ad Choices" privacy program has made life harder for ad agencies. AdAge's Kate Kaye writes, "Depending on the size of the ad campaign, it can take anywhere from five to 20 hours of work [for Vivaki] to produce a required compliance report if the agency doesn't use a centralized system... 'We need the publishers to adopt the industry standard. We cannot have everyone embrace it in their own flavor,' says Vivaki SVP Grace Liau." More. <http://r20.rs6.net/tn.jsp?e=001VjdUGZ86zYrMQ_MPtpgWI2IfJa3Rae0I8vN02KROuyqKnxqjuO7RJZJA4BkfWq802Chu3qoK1LVdBgDEylPWEB3L2tiL-9qBPY7W2_vnSKmCW1ugI56ubqvctHwiOnfnBEFjc7C2GGqcJ33xFz_a7TET7biQfn9E29P_ZFQddp2_brCNYFdstGGX0Z3JYb8my5wDEEAi61h9EkecWoWYk77-5nbs7U17>  

Tapping The Mobile Cloud 

The M&A frenzy around ad-related cloud computing services shows no signs of slowing down. Just before 2012 ended, Phunware, the enterprise mobile cloud systems provider, acquired mobile ad company TapIt Media Group for $23 million. Read the release <http://r20.rs6.net/tn.jsp?e=001VjdUGZ86zYq9j1zvVfZPs0-dBY0VbKqRkJBf0WQRpoeFqJAVOKxBQehIoIXPKNtc83Zn2R_h8a3xW3d71Bmuqo5_4SzC9Whx3EyEmWFtG2U6iU9RFtHRATUNO8xKIu7dLMqHCOhtJBCLma15qY7t4B12rXWvI62-mmkudiJrwbYLU9bdsIOMY9gr6movk1je> . TapIt specifically provides self-serve ad buys, real-time bidding, cross-platform ad creation and a range of supply-side tools to its network of about 30,000 active publishers, notes Techcrunch's Frederic Lardinois, who quotes of TapIt CEO Giancarlo Maniaci, as saying "With the velocity of adoption and maturation of mobile increasing daily, we strongly believe that fully integrated, easy to use, simple to deploy and all-inclusive mobile platforms like Phunware's MaaS will soon define both 'best of breed' and the new global mobile standard." Read more <http://r20.rs6.net/tn.jsp?e=001VjdUGZ86zYoSoSryzsU14mryLs_2O1sIlDz9-YPg5U1QKAt2wSwMoVVH3s_obgfaJsi41fgkXGq-lea9EgnlYGhARlYyngep7n74JvQtUwMPeUlDB4zO2WoucNohBT4fo3hQrKBhb21WdCC900KdNXxoK2OHENMcZXMPguvTIHHf_RzIm1ksKrZTn3xECxEKj9f3w-jCR8LR7YwAE1IfVA4LVNWe05gA3XNSTg7ws64=> . 

Overnight Success In 36 Months 

The idea of "build it and they will come" doesn't work when applied to the online publishing business and advertising. And woe to those who take the phrase "overnight success" literally. It's more like "over half-a-year success," writes Business Insider's CRO Pete Spande writes on his personal blog. In advising digital publishers on the five stages they'll probably experience in some form, Spande says that even if you've got everything right on paper, there are no sure things. "The history of the Internet is littered with great products that never found a winning ad model." Read more <http://r20.rs6.net/tn.jsp?e=001VjdUGZ86zYohdxgpKeZLFDVR1eGW9pg9KSuNEbvz3uaeJHzRcmQJA_iMl2q0PF0JUt_yLLoey6Ihv1qgkeiKkXgHKRr4tBQaB3lrIsw2eCEsNd-jzz8-Y9IO4s7DrEjpXPai1vgX-_9-1ZC18VXw7_dqA-TfwRgRW848H8n0SlsNn1PnPXfPSGn39IThYBvcVTjJT_YIQcJMcKg2QSj3b1gw1Y8J93gXRCW4tZcSZTQ=> .

Buying platform Marin Software, who's early claim to fame was in the search engine marketing space along with Kenshoo and Efficient Frontier (acquired by Adobe in 2011 <http://r20.rs6.net/tn.jsp?e=001jFY0_jyDQiMLeF3zkefV9iBjgn_41RXvEfSzqaw6DDde774m3ys8byYceGGK1I_SEW24-RpXPFCvxuA3bBuH8Fig6U5kfK0UAJqFqo7fBLPYkJ84fikd6A12iYcuF-hg3xC99CjoTCjxalnZ26pOGR6KIcZZIcQOP1I95IO1t8_7tV3LboAFspRLQ4ZmBrSbVNE37SVeqBA=> ), says that after taking over $1000 million in funding, the next step is an initial public offering. Read more in MediaPost <http://r20.rs6.net/tn.jsp?e=001jFY0_jyDQiOGUqUtE1Zq8Apdvn3kug9jyknhSBNNMA-umbRYgXyT8nXLKscUIXTyw5KWUIIDIVkucOG59AZOSFtrPcJaHxD_DOop0cvO5k2DbkSxh26sBbwx_dmWpuEzlrltB8lb9g1Me9lNE2SgkdRLIciFZ1HFaaZyg-RtAHp85iNdRbag4H4A163phZ4tyTjw7Td4AF0=> . How many private ad tech companies will be saying "IPO" this year?

Holiday Acquisition 

WPP Group's Kantar Media announced on December 21 the acquisition of Chicago-based analytics firm AdGooroo. Kantar North America CEO Terry Kent said in a release that "the acquisition will enable a more holistic approach to measurement of the digital media landscape, broadening Kantar Media's current methodic insight into display, video, ad networks and paid search advertising trends - including expenditure allocated, and keywords purchased - as well as detailed data on spend, impressions, creative, traffic and site usage." AdGooroo claims 400 marketer clients and 35 employees. Read more. <http://r20.rs6.net/tn.jsp?e=001jFY0_jyDQiOk7uC_4ySVV3oo6_NPsC7FupX-QhzP2NIDSPzdX7_U5yeQazMzZNeA0b6puqLwjxZZfo4BDxTA5Ov7QRlqeRUgo8fcvkuGoOwuQxIH1Tm0fCVISsK2wK1nsPGZUoztw8hOg22OMXMU5GYve6ogs5VVnJi0NMM6t2f5BoxsLi-JXLuPTgvajJZY>  Attribution buzz builds. 

Chinese FBX 

Chinese buying platform iPinYou says it has real-time bidding to access to the Facebook Exchange. iPinYou CEO Huang Xiaonan tells China Daily, "There is demand from Chinese advertisers to reach out to US consumers and this is how Facebook can cash in on the Chinese market." China demand-side platforms targeting chinese consumers - Facebook's revenue footprint continues to expand. Read more. <http://r20.rs6.net/tn.jsp?e=001jFY0_jyDQiPuf-0XMilKOS114ReLZzGPxI5DzcoEgLpeTkaDV3rbwpqB6IJlwAZl5SRtThVh8i_kLWWDzl1m1NCPPlWZdfQTFzCRs7T3vzIcPVwOemuxa53RxkBN8hnYG8rqTXoxYoWAwluI7KNbUJgCEaUu1pEKPWb1McVSZeTv_SW2e1Au_g==>  

One Product, Two Prices 

The new era of marketing personalization has brought its share of bogeymen. Among the most frequently invoked has been price variability, where two users are quoted different prices based on data attributes. The Wall Street Journal tracks down specific examples from Staples. The newspaper "found that the Staples Inc. website displays different prices to people after estimating their locations. More than that, Staples appeared to consider the person's distance from a rival brick-and-mortar store, either OfficeMax Inc. or Office Depot Inc. If rival stores were within 20 miles or so, Staples.com usually showed a discounted price." Read more (subscription). <http://r20.rs6.net/tn.jsp?e=001jFY0_jyDQiPl3CLhZP1IxlxXllQVAIYCJheHc60d3ZEJDQI5sSGGSNQ1lvEizD597yEtvRa_NxlhC1XBHDkuWw4DJax3rXUvs5exchz7wn9uedJIOkMvffwbwiENx06W5IINKW3-XCSHzFbjz1zXJPERGJkM7-u7WlA3oBA1lNfuGhd70-nI6iX9TQLdyYjc6FV4VDdGeSnNDkTUrcnSc95e-4Ets7Dq9Pzk03GxsOc=>  

Foursquare PII 

Foursquare will expose more data about users, including their full names, under a privacy policy change slated for January 28. As for venue owners, TheNextWeb notes, "Currently, they can see check-ins at their locations from the past three hours, as well as location 'mayors'... when the new policy comes into effect, Foursquare says that it will allow them to see "more of those recent check-ins, instead of just three hours worth." In other words, augmenting first party data. More. <http://r20.rs6.net/tn.jsp?e=001jFY0_jyDQiN2I-P2M_4ZUjaulvXViRrJ5UGzg9RCTu1gz3AwlE1WDtdNJYjFkQg9b0uV3OmvFoVxdk-7-w49cD787clrbvjgpNAiCDGf7mMFYJ9aRj60AoX5uMUTbOFY1RUstjqRXulfStEsrmPhr235aABFvvRcW-HYfZiIphP_ONkDPgvDuZzo2X6ZLzgkqGU5JThDFo8Cy2X9cpMKtA==>
